Women's Testimony in Non-Hudud Rights
States the rule and proof for testimony in rights other than hudud and qisas

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on testimony in rights other than hudud and qisas, and explain the Quranic proof and its extension.

Core Idea
In all rights except hudud and qisas, testimony of one man and two women is accepted, based on Quran 2:282.

This lesson examines the Hanafi position on women's testimony: it is accepted in all financial and non-financial rights, unlike hudud and qisas where women's testimony is excluded. The ruling is derived from the general applicability of the reason (illah) in the Quranic verse on transactions.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and ruling
The act is giving testimony (shahada) in a right that is not hudud or qisas. The ruling is that such testimony is accepted from two men or one man and two women.
The ruling covers both financial rights (e.g., sale) and non-financial rights (e.g., marriage, divorce).
2
Locate the dalil
The primary proof is Quran 2:282, which explicitly allows one man and two women in place of two male witnesses in transactions.
The verse is in the context of debt transactions, but Hanafis extend it to all non-hudud rights.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
The verse states that a man and two women are acceptable so that if one woman errs, the other can remind her. This reason (forgetfulness) is general, so the rule applies to all matters where testimony is needed, except hudud and qisas where a stricter standard is maintained.
Hanafi usul: a text's ruling extends beyond its immediate context to all cases sharing the same illah (effective cause).
4
Note the ikhtilaf
Some other schools (e.g., Shafi'i) restrict women's testimony to financial matters only, arguing the verse is specific to transactions.
Hanafis respond that the illah (prevention of error) is universal, and companion practice supports broader acceptance.
5
Confirm the mufta bihi
The Hanafi position, accepted by all three imams (Abu Hanifa, Abu Yusuf, Muhammad), is that women's testimony is valid in all non-hudud rights.
This is the relied-upon view for fatwa.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
[۲۸۱۵] (۶) اور جو ان کے علاوہ ہوں حقوق میں سے تو قبول کی جائے گی ان میں دو مردوں کی گواہی یا ایک مرد اور دو عورتوں کی گواہی۔ چاہے حق مال ہو یا غیر مال ہو۔ مثلا نکاح، طلاق، وکالت، وصیت ۔ ی حدود اور قصاص کے علاوہ جتنے حقوق ہیں چاہے وہ حقوق مالی ہوں یا حقوق غیر مالی ہوں ان سب میں مرد کے ساتھ عورتوں کی گواہی بھی مقبول ہے۔ مثلا معاملات، بیج ہے، شراء ہے ، نکاح ، طلاق، وکالت اور وصیت ہے ان سب میں عورتوں کی گواہی بھی مقبول ہے۔ آیت میں اس کا ثبوت ہے۔ واستشهدوا شهيدين من رج من رجالك فان لم يكونا رجلين فرجل وامرأتان ممن ترضون من الشهداء ان تضل احداهما الاخرى (ب) ( آیت ۲۸۲ ، سورۃ البقرۃ ۲) اس آیت میں ہے کہ دو مرد نہ ہوں تو ایک مرد اور دو عورتوں کی گواہی قابل قبول ہے۔ یہ آیت چونکہ معاملات کے سلسلے میں ہے اس لئے تمام ہی معاملات میں عورتوں کی گواہی مقبول ہوگی (۲) حاشیہ : (پچھلے صفحہ سے آگے ) کے بعد دونوں خلیفوں کے زمانے سے سنت جاری ہے کہ حدود میں عورتوں کی گواہی جائز نہیں ہے (الف) حضرت علی نے فرمایا کہ عورتوں کی گواہی طلاق، نکاح ، حدود اور قصاص میں جائز نہیں ہے ( ب ) تمہارے دو مردوں کی گواہی لو۔ پس اگر مرد نہ ہوں تو ایک مرد اور دو عورتیں جن کی گواہی سے تم راضی ہوتا کہ ایک بھول جائے تو ایک دوسری کو یاد دلائے۔
And whatever other than those are among rights, then it will be accepted: in them, the testimony of two men, or one man and two women. Whether it is a property right or non-property right, such as marriage, divorce, agency, and will. That is, all rights besides hudud and qisas, whether financial or non-financial, in all of them women's testimony with men is accepted. For example, transactions, sale, purchase, marriage, divorce, agency, and will—in all of these women's testimony is accepted. The proof is in the verse: 'And bring two witnesses from among your men; and if two men are not available, then one man and two women from those you approve of the witnesses, so that if one of them errs, the other may remind her.' (Surah Al-Baqarah 2:282) In this verse it says that if two men are not available, then one man and two women are acceptable. Since this verse is in the context of transactions, therefore in all transactions women's testimony will be accepted. Footnote: The practice from the Prophet and the two caliphs is that women's testimony is not permissible in hudud. Ali said that women's testimony is not permissible in divorce, marriage, hudud, and qisas.
Source pages p. 141

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof for testimony in all rights other than hudud and qisas. The rule is that testimony is accepted from two men or from one man and two women, for both financial and non-financial rights such as marriage, divorce, agency, and will. The proof is the Quranic verse (2:282) which is in the context of financial transactions but is extended to all non-hudud rights because the reason (illah) for accepting women's testimony is their need to be reminded due to forgetfulness, which applies generally. The footnote reiterates that in hudud and qisas, women's testimony is not accepted, confirming the distinction.

Key Terms
حقوق غير مالية (huquq ghayr maliyyah): Non-financial rights such as marriage, divorce, agency.
تضل احداهما (tadilla ihdahuma): One of the two women errs or forgets, which is the reason given in the verse for needing two women.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) Only in hudud cases like theft
B) In all rights except hudud and qisas
C) Only in financial transactions
D) Only in marriage and divorce

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi fiqh, women's testimony is accepted in all rights except hudud and qisas, based on Quran 2:282 and the general applicability of the illah.

Testimony in Hudud and Qisas: Only Men Accepted
Ruling on inadmissibility of women's testimony in Hudud and Qisas with proofs

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling that women's testimony is not accepted in Hudud and Qisas and identify the textual proofs (mursal hadith and athar of Ali) that support it.

Core Idea
Women's testimony is rejected in Hudud and Qisas because these punishments are dropped by doubt and women are considered unreliable by textual proof.

This lesson presents a core rule of Islamic evidence law: the admissibility of testimony varies by case type. In Hudud and Qisas, Hanafi law requires two male witnesses; women's testimony is not accepted. The following passage from Al-Sharh al-Thamiri provides the ruling and its scriptural foundations.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is testimony in Hudud and Qisas cases. Ruling: only two men's testimony accepted; women's testimony not accepted.
2
Locate the first proof
A mursal hadith transmitted without a chain states women's testimony is not allowed in Hudud and blood (Qisas).
Mursal hadith is considered weak (zanni al-thubut) but acceptable when supported by other evidence.
3
Locate the second proof
The athar of Ali ibn Abi Talib explicitly states that women's testimony is not permissible in divorce, marriage, Hudud, and blood (meaning Qisas).
Recorded in Musannaf Abd al-Razzaq.
4
Understand the Hanafi position and its authority
This is the position of the Hanafi school, deemed from Zahir al-Riwayah. No known intra-madhhab dispute. The ruling is mufta bihi.
Other schools may accept women's testimony in some Hudud, but Hanafi rejects entirely.

الشرح الثميرى الجزء الرابع ۱۳۴ كتاب الشهادات ) الرجال ولا تقبل فيها شهادة النساء [۲۴] (۵) ومنها الشهادة ببقية الحدود والقصاص تقبل فيها شهادة رجلين ولا تقبل فيها شهادة النساء [ ۲۸۱۵] (٢) وما سوى ذلك من خامس جس ۵۲۸ نمبر ۲۸۷۰۵ / مصنف عبد الرزاق، باب هل تجوز شهادة النساء مع الرجال في الحدود و غیره؟ ، ج علامن، ص ۱۳۳۰، نمبر ۱۵۴۱۲ر سفن للمبتی ، باب شہادة في الطلاق والرجعة و مافی معنا هما من النكاح والقصاص والحدود، ج عاشر ص ۲۵۰ نمبر ۲۰۵۲۸) اس حدیث مرسل اور اثر سے معلوم ہوا کہ حدود میں عورتوں کی گواہی مقبول نہیں ہے۔ [۲۸۱۴] (۵) ان سے شہادت ہے باقی حدود کی اور قصاص کی کہ ان میں دو مردوں کی گواہی قبول کی جاتی ہے اور ان میں عورتوں کی گواہی قبول نہیں کی جاتی۔ از نا میں تو چار مردوں کی گواہی چاہئے۔ ان میں عورتوں کی گواہی مقبول نہیں ہے۔ اور باقی حدود اور قصاص میں بھی عورتوں کی گواہی قبول نہیں کی جائے گی۔ صرف مردوں کی گواہی قبول کی جائے گی۔ حدود کے بارے میں او پر حدیث مرسل گزر چکی۔ قصاص بھی اسی درجے کا ہے اس لئے قصاص میں بھی عورت کی گواہی مقبول نہیں ہے (۲) اس اثر میں بھی اس کا ثبوت ہے۔ ان علی بن ابی طالب قال لا تجوز شهادة النساء في الطلاق والنكاح والحدود والدماء (الف) (مصنف عبدالرزاق، باب هل تجوز شهادة النساء مع الرجال في الحدود وغيره ؟ ، ج ثامن ، ص ۱۳۲۹، نمبر ۱۵۴۰۵/مصنف ابن الي هيتة ١٠٩ ء في شهادة النساء في الحدود، ج خامس ص ۵۲۸ نمبر ۲۸۷۱۱) اس اثر میں دم سے مراد قصاص ہے۔ اس سے معلوم ہوا کہ قصاص میں بھی عورتوں کی گواہی مقبول نہیں ہے (۳) آیت میں عورت کے بارے میں بتایا کہ ایک دوسرے کو یاد دلائے جس سے معلوم ہوا کہ عورتوں میں نسیان ہے۔ اور حدود اور قصاص شبہ سے بھی ساقط ہو جاتے ہیں۔ اس لئے بھی عورت کی گواہی حدود اور قصاص میں مقبول نہیں ہے۔ حاشیہ : (پچھلے صفحہ سے آگے ) کے بعد دونوں خلیفوں کے زمانے سے سنت جاری ہے کہ حدود میں عورتوں کی گواہی جائز نہیں ہے (الف) حضرت علی نے فرمایا کہ عورتوں کی گواہی طلاق، نکاح ، حدود اور قصاص میں جائز نہیں ہے ( ب ) تمہارے دو مردوں کی گواہی لو۔ پس اگر مرد نہ ہوں تو ایک مرد اور دو عورتیں جن کی گواہی سے تم راضی ہوتا کہ ایک بھول جائے تو ایک دوسری کو یاد دلائے۔
The text begins: 'Men, and women's testimony is not accepted in it. And from among them is testimony for the rest of the Hudud and Qisas: in them, the testimony of two men is accepted, and women's testimony is not accepted.' Then the commentary explains that this is based on a mursal hadith and the athar of Ali who said, 'Women's testimony is not allowed in divorce, marriage, Hudud, and blood (meaning Qisas).' The commentary also cites the Quranic verse about forgetfulness to support the reasoning that women's testimony is not reliable in matters where doubt can drop the punishment.
Source pages p. 141

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof. The author states the ruling: in Hudud (fixed punishments) and Qisas (retaliation), only the testimony of two men is accepted; women's testimony is not. He provides three proofs: (1) a mursal hadith indicating women's testimony is accepted in some matters but not Hudud, (2) the athar of Ali (رضي الله عنه) explicitly excluding women from testifying in Hudud and Qisas (here 'blood' means Qisas), and (3) a rational argument from the Quranic verse (2:282) which mentions women's forgetfulness, combined with the principle that Hudud and Qisas are dropped by any doubt, so women's testimony is insufficient. The footnote adds that the practice of the two caliphs (Abu Bakr and Umar) continued this ruling. This is the position of the Hanafi school.

Key Terms
حدود (hudud): Fixed punishments prescribed by Allah for specific crimes like theft, zina, etc.
قصاص (qisas): Retaliatory punishment for murder or injury, equivalent to the harm caused.
شهادة (shahada): Testimony given in court to prove a claim.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Why is women's testimony not accepted in Hudud and Qisas according to the Hanafi school?
A) Because women are inherently unreliable
B) Because Hudud and Qisas are dropped by doubts, and women are prone to forgetfulness
C) Because the Quran explicitly forbids women's testimony in all cases
D) Because only prophets can testify in Hudud

Key Takeaway
In Hudud and Qisas, the Hanafi school strictly requires two male witnesses; women's testimony is rejected based on explicit texts and the principle that these punishments are dropped by doubt.

The Rational Proof: Forgetfulness and Shubha in Hudud and Qisas
Rational proof for excluding women's testimony in Hudud and Qisas

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the Hanafi rational argument from Quranic forgetfulness (2:282) and the principle that hudud and qisas are dropped by doubt to exclude women's testimony.

Core Idea
Women's testimony is unreliable in hudud because hudud drop by any doubt, and women are described as prone to forgetfulness in the Quran.

Beyond the explicit hadith, the Hanafi school also employs a rational argument derived from Quran 2:282 and the legal maxim that hudud and qisas are suspended upon any uncertainty. This lesson explores that reasoning and how it reinforces the textual proofs.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Quranic basis
The verse about debt (2:282) mentions two male witnesses or one man and two women, and explains that if one woman forgets, the other reminds her. This indicates a tendency toward forgetfulness (nasyan) in women.
Quran 2:282: '...that if one of them (the women) errs, the other can remind her.'
2
Understand the principle that hudud and qisas drop by doubt
In Hanafi fiqh, hudud and qisas are averted by any shubha (doubt). Therefore, evidence must be certain; women's testimony, due to forgetfulness, lacks that certainty.
Principle: 'Hudud are dropped by doubts' (al-hudud tusqatu bi al-shubuhat).
3
Connect forgetfulness to the requirement of certainty
Since hudud and qisas lead to severe punishments (hudud are fixed, qisas retaliation), certainty is essential. The described forgetfulness makes women's testimony insufficient.
4
Derive the Hanafi ruling
Combining the textual and rational proofs, women's testimony is not accepted in hudud and qisas. This is the mufta bihi position.
The rational proof reinforces the textual proof.

Women's Testimony in Rights: Hanafi vs Shafi'i
Ruling on acceptance of women's testimony in rights other than Hudud and Qisas, with inter-madhhab dispute

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi and Shafi'i positions on women's testimony in non-financial rights, identify the proofs each school uses, and explain the practical consequence of the dispute.

Core Idea
In Hanafi fiqh, one man and two women can testify in all rights except Hudud and Qisas.

This passage addresses a classic inter-madhhab dispute on the scope of women's testimony. The matn states the Hanafi rule: in all rights (financial or non-financial) except Hudud and Qisas, testimony of two men or one man and two women is accepted. The commentary then presents the Shafi'i restriction and the supporting evidence. Understanding this dispute clarifies how each school interprets the Quranic verse and the practice of the Companions.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Hanafi position
State the Hanafi ruling from the matn: testimony of one man and two women is accepted in all rights (financial and non-financial) except Hudud and Qisas. Examples include marriage, divorce, agency, and will.
The passage explicitly lists marriage (نكاح), divorce (طلاق), agency (وكالة), and bequest (وصية) as non-financial rights.
2
Locate the Hanafi dalil
The primary proof is Quran 2:282, which is general for all transactions. The commentary also cites the practice of Umar (رضي الله عنه) accepting one man and women in marriage.
The Quranic verse uses the phrase 'فَرَجُلٌ وَامْرَأَتَانِ' (one man and two women) in the context of financial transactions, but the Hanafi school extends it to all rights.
3
State the Shafi'i position and its dalil
Imam al-Shafi'i restricts women's testimony to financial matters and their derivatives (توابع). He cites the athar of Ali (رضي الله عنه) that women's testimony is not accepted in marriage, divorce, and Hudud.
The athar is explicitly quoted: 'لاتجوز شهادة النساء في الطلاق والنكاح والحدود'.
4
Analyze the Hanafi response
The Hanafi school responds that the Quranic verse is general and takes precedence over the athar. The athar of Ali is interpreted as limited to Hudud and Qisas, or is overruled by the practice of Umar.
The passage does not explicitly rebut the Shafi'i dalil, but the Hanafi position remains based on the generality of the Quran and the stronger evidence from Umar's practice.
5
Identify the practical consequence (thamarah al-khilaf)
In Hanafi, a marriage can be proven by one man and two women; in Shafi'i, it cannot. This affects the burden of proof in family law cases.
The dispute directly impacts everyday legal practice: which party wins the case depends on the school applied.

[۲۸۱۵] (۶) اور جو ان کے علاوہ ہوں حقوق میں سے تو قبول کی جائے گی ان میں دو مردوں کی گواہی یا ایک مرد اور دو عورتوں کی گواہی۔ چاہے حق مال ہو یا غیر مال ہو۔ مثلا نکاح، طلاق، وکالت، وصیت ۔ ی حدود اور قصاص کے علاوہ جتنے حقوق ہیں چاہے وہ حقوق مالی ہوں یا حقوق غیر مالی ہوں ان سب میں مرد کے ساتھ عورتوں کی گواہی بھی مقبول ہے۔ مثلا معاملات، بیج ہے، شراء ہے ، نکاح ، طلاق، وکالت اور وصیت ہے ان سب میں عورتوں کی گواہی بھی مقبول ہے۔ آیت میں اس کا ثبوت ہے۔ واستشهدوا شهيدين من رج من رجالكم فان لم يكونا رجلين فرجل وامرأتان ممن ترضون من الشهداء ان تضل احداهما الاخرى (ب) ( آیت ۲۸۲ ، سورۃ البقرۃ ۲) اس آیت میں ہے کہ دو مرد نہ ہوں تو ایک مرد اور دو عورتوں کی گواہی قابل قبول ہے۔ یہ آیت چونکہ معاملات کے سلسلے میں ہے اس لئے تمام ہی معاملات میں عورتوں کی گواہی مقبول ہوگی (۲) 
الحقوق تُقبل فيها شهادة رجلين او رجل وامرأتين سواء كان الحق مالا او غير مال مثل النكاح والطلاق والوكالة والوصية
اثر میں ہے۔ ان عمر بن ال بن الخطاب اجاز شهادة رجل واحد مع نساء فى نكاح (الف) (مصنف عبدالرزاق، باب هل تجوز شهادة النساء مع الرجال في الحدود وغيره ؟ ، ج ثامن، ص ۱۵۴۱۶،۳۳۱ر مصنف ابن ابی شیبه ، ۳۹۷ في شهادة النساء في العتق والدين والطلاق ، ج رابع مس ۵۱۷، نمبر ۲۲۶۸ دار قطنی ، کتاب الاقضیة والاحکام، ج رابع ص ۱۴۹، نمبر ۴۵۱۳) اس اثر سے معلوم ہوا کہ طلاق نکاح وغیرہ میں بھی عورتوں کی گواہی مقبول ہے۔
امام شافعی فرماتے ہیں کہ مال اور اس کے توابع میں عورتوں کی گواہی مقبول ہے۔ نکاح، طلاق غیرہ میں نہیں۔
او پر اثر گزرا۔ ان علی بن ابی طالب قال لاتجوز شهادة النساء في الطلاق والنكاح والحدود (ب)(مصنف عبد الرزاق، باب هل تجوز شهادة النساء مع الرجال في الحدود و غیره ؟ ، ج ثامن، ص ۱۳۲۹، نمبر ۱۵۴۰۵ار مصنف ابن ابی شبیه ۰۹ فى شهادة النساء في الحدود ، ج خامس، ص ۵۲۸ نمبر ۲۸۷۰۷ سفن اللبیہقی ، باب الشهادة في الطلاق والرحمة وما في معناهما من النكاح والقصاص والحدود، ج عاشر ص ۲۵۰، نمبر ۲۰۵۲۸) اس اثر سے معلوم ہوا کہ عورت کی گواہی طلاق اور نکاح میں بھی مقبول نہیں ہے۔ اس لئے وہ صرف دین میں گواہی دے سکتی ہے۔
The commentary says: 'And other than those (Hudud and Qisas) among rights, the testimony of two men or one man and two women is accepted, whether the right is financial or non-financial, such as marriage, divorce, agency, bequest.' It then cites the Quranic verse (2:282) as proof and the practice of Umar who accepted one man and women in marriage. Then it mentions that Imam Shafi'i holds that women's testimony is only accepted in financial matters and their derivatives, not in marriage and divorce. The text then cites the athar of Ali which states women's testimony is not accepted in divorce, marriage, and Hudud, concluding that women can only testify in matters of religion (din).
Source pages p. 141

Commentary
This passage is an inter-madhhab dispute. The Hanafi position, stated in the matn, is that in all rights other than Hudud and Qisas (whether financial like sale and purchase, or non-financial like marriage, divorce, agency, will), the testimony of two men or one man and two women is accepted. The proof is the Quranic verse (2:282) which is general for all transactions. The commentary supports this with the practice of Umar (رضي الله عنه) who accepted one man with women in marriage. Then the Shafi'i view is presented: women's testimony is only accepted in financial matters and their derivatives, not in marriage and divorce. The Hanafi response is implicit: the Quranic verse is general and the athar of Umar contradicts the Shafi'i restriction. The text then cites the athar of Ali which seems to support the Shafi'i view, but the Hanafi position is that this athar is limited to Hudud and Qisas as per the explicit wording? Actually the commentary presents the athar of Ali without explicit rebuttal, but the Hanafi stance is based on the broader application of the Quran and the practice of Umar. The operative ruling (mufta bihi) is the Hanafi position.

Key Terms
حقوق (huquq): Rights or claims that can be litigated, including financial and non-financial.
توابع (tawabi'): Derivatives or ancillary matters related to financial rights.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) It is accepted with two women and one man
B) It is not accepted at all
C) It is accepted only if no men are available
D) It is accepted in marriage but not divorce

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school accepts the testimony of one man and two women in all rights except Hudud and Qisas, based on the general implication of Quran 2:282 and the practice of Umar.

Shahadat — Testimony

Single Woman's Testimony in Exclusive Female Matters
Ruling with proof on single woman testimony

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on the testimony of a single woman in childbirth, virginity, and hidden defects, and identify the hadith proofs supporting it.

Core Idea
In matters men cannot see, one woman's testimony suffices — necessity overrides the general rule.

The general rule in Islamic law requires two women (or one man and two women) for testimony in most cases. However, for matters that are exclusively within women's knowledge — such as childbirth, virginity, and hidden defects — the Hanafi school accepts the testimony of a single woman. This lesson examines the ruling, its rationale, and the prophetic proofs that establish this exception.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Rulings
Read the matn and commentary to list the three specific matters where one woman's testimony is accepted: childbirth, virginity, and hidden defects (especially of private parts).
These are matters men cannot normally witness.
2
Understand the Rationale
The commentary explains that men cannot see women giving birth (except his wife or slave-girl) and cannot examine virginity or private defects. Therefore, only women's testimony is possible.
Necessity (darurah) and customary practice (urf) support this exception.
3
Examine the First Proof
The hadith of Huzayfah (or the midwife) states the Prophet accepted the testimony of a midwife. This directly proves the ruling for childbirth.
The hadith is ahad but sufficient for practice.
4
Examine the Second Proof
The hadith of the slave-girl who testified about breastfeeding: the Prophet accepted her testimony and separated the couple. This extends the ruling to similar exclusive female matters.
Breastfeeding is also a matter men cannot directly observe.
5
Synthesize the Ruling
Combine the two proofs to establish that for any matter that men cannot normally see (e.g., childbirth, virginity, hidden defects, breastfeeding), one woman's testimony is sufficient and judgement is based on it.
This is the mufta bihi position with no intra-Hanafi dispute.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وتقبل فى الولادة والبكارة والعيوب [۲۸۱۶](۷) ولادت اور باکرہ ہونے میں اور عورتوں کے ان جگہ کے عیوب میں جہاں مرد مطلع نہیں ہو سکتے ایک عورت کی گواہی قبول کی جائے گی۔ بچہ پیدا ہوتے وقت مرد بیوی اور باندی کے علاوہ عورتوں کو نہیں دیکھ سکتا ۔ اسی طرح عورت باکرہ ہے یا نہیں مرد اس کو نہیں دیکھ سکتا۔ اس لئے جہاں مرد نہیں دیکھ سکتا ہو وہاں صرف عورتوں کی گواہی قبول کی جائے گی۔ اسی طرح شرمگاہ و غیرہ کی بیماری جس پر مرد مطلع نہیں ہو سکتا اس کے بارے میں ایک عورت کی گا ہی کافی مانی جائے گی۔ اور اسی پر فیصلہ کیا جائے گا۔
(1) حدیث میں ہے کہ ایک دائی کی گواہی مقبول ہے۔ عن حذيفة ان رسول الله لا الله اجاز شهادة القابلة (ج) ( درقطنی، کتاب الاقضیۃ والا حکام، ج رابع ص ۱۴۹ نمبر ۴۵۱۱ رسن للبیہقی ، باب ماجاء فی عددهن (ای عدد النساء)، ج عاشر ص ۲۵۴ نمبر ۲۰۵۴۲) اس حدیث سے معلوم ہوا کہ دائی کی گواہی مقبول ہے (۲) حدیث میں ہے کہ باندی نے دودھ پلانے کی گواہی دی تو اس کی وجہ سے زکار ج توڑ دیا۔ حدثني عقبة بن الحارث او سمعته منه انه تزوج ام يحيى بنت ابی اهاب قال فجاءت امة سوداء فقالت قد ارضعتكما فذكرت ذلك للنبی الا الله فاعرض عنى قال فتنحيت فذكرت ذلك له قال وكيف وقد زعمت انها قد
حاشیہ : (الف) حضرت عمر نے عورتوں کے ساتھ ایک مرد کی گواہی جائز قرار دی نکاح میں (ب) حضرت علی نے فرمایا عورتوں کی گواہی جائز نہیں ہے طلاق ، نکاح اور حدود میں (ج) آپ نے دائی کی گواہی کی اجازت دی یعنی اس کو قبول فرمایا۔
The matn says: 'And it is accepted in childbirth, virginity, and defects.' The commentary: 'In childbirth, virginity, and defects of women's private parts that men cannot see, the testimony of one woman is accepted. Because a man cannot see women other than his wife or slave-girl at the time of birth. Similarly, a man cannot determine if a woman is a virgin. Therefore, where a man cannot see, only women's testimony is accepted. Similarly for diseases of the private parts that men cannot access, one woman's testimony is sufficient and judgement is based on it. (1) The hadith that a midwife's testimony is accepted. (2) The hadith of the slave-girl who testified about breastfeeding and the Prophet acted upon it.' The footnote explains references.
Source pages p. 142

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof. The matn states the ruling: the testimony of one woman is accepted in matters of childbirth, virginity, and hidden defects (including illnesses of the private parts) because these are matters that men cannot normally witness. The commentary elaborates that men cannot see women giving birth except his wife or slave-girl, and cannot examine virginity or private defects. Therefore, a single woman's testimony is sufficient and judgement is based on it. Two proofs are given: (1) a hadith that the Prophet accepted the testimony of a midwife, and (2) a hadith where a slave-girl's testimony about breastfeeding was accepted and the Prophet separated the couple. This ruling is specific to the Hanafi school and is based on necessity and customary practice.

Key Terms
ولادة (wiladah): Childbirth, including proof of lineage or parentage.
بكارة (bakarah): Virginity, a matter that cannot be verified by men.
عيوب (uyub): Physical defects or illnesses, especially of private parts.

Key Terms from Source Passage

B) A marriage contract
C) The occurrence of childbirth
D) A case of theft

Key Takeaway
In matters exclusively known to women, a single woman's testimony is sufficient by necessity and Sunnah.

Shahadat — Testimony
intermediate

Women's Testimony in All Rights: Hanafi vs Shafi'i
General ruling on women's testimony in rights with inter-madhhab dispute

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi position that women's testimony is accepted in all rights (including marriage and divorce) and evaluate the Shafi'i counter-argument using the evidence of Umar and Ali.

Core Idea
Women's testimony is accepted in all rights, not just financial — the Hanafi school relies on the practice of Umar.

The Hanafi school holds that women's testimony is admissible in all types of rights (huquq), whether financial or non-financial, such as marriage, divorce, agency, and wills. This position, supported by the practice of Caliph Umar, is contested by Imam al-Shafi'i, who restricts women's testimony to financial matters. In this lesson, we examine the proofs and the practical implications of this difference.

Guided Path
1
State the general Hanafi rule on women's testimony in rights
Identify that the Hanafi school accepts testimony of two men or one man and two women in all rights, both mal and non-mal (e.g., nikah, talaq).
This is the default ruling from Zahir al-Riwayah.
2
Present the Hanafi evidence from Umar's practice
The athar from Umar ibn al-Khattab shows he accepted testimony of one man with women in a marriage case. This is a key proof for Hanafis.
Refer to the narration in Musannaf Abd al-Razzaq.
3
State the Shafi'i opposing view and its evidence
Imam al-Shafi'i limits women's testimony to property matters, citing the narration from Ali ibn Abi Talib that women's testimony is not allowed in talaq, nikah, and hudud.
Ali's narration is found in multiple sources.
4
Analyze the Hanafi response to the Shafi'i evidence
The Hanafi school responds that Ali's narration is either weak or abrogated by Umar's practice and other evidence. They prioritize stronger proofs.
The hadith of the midwife and slave-woman also support the Hanafi view.
5
Determine the practical consequence (thamarah al-khilaf)
Under Hanafi law, marriage and divorce can be proven by one man and two women; under Shafi'i law, two men are required, and women's testimony is not accepted at all in these matters.
This difference affects court proceedings in practice.

حاشیہ : (الف) عقبہ بن حارث سے سنا کہ انہوں نے ام کی بنت ابی اہاب سے شادی کی ، فرماتے ہیں کہ ایک کالی باندی آئی اور کہنے لگی کہ میں نے تم دونوں کو دودھ پلایا ہے۔ میں نے اس کا تذکرہ حضور صلى الله عليه وسلم سے کیا تو آپ نے مجھ سے اعراض کر لیا۔ میں نے دوسرے کنارے جا کر پھر اس کا تذکرہ کیا تو آپ نے فرمایا کیسے ہوگا ؟ وہ باندی گمان کرتی ہے کہ تم دونوں کو دودھ پلایا ہے؟ پھر آپ نے اس عورت سے روک دیا (ب) حضرت شعیمی سے روایت ہے کہ لوگ فرماتے ہیں کہ ایک عورت کی گواہی وہاں جائز ہے جہاں مرد مطلع نہ ہو سکتے ہوں (ج) حضرت عطاء فرماتے ہیں کہ ولادت میں چار عورتوں کے بغیر گواہی جائز نہیں (د) تم میں سے یعنی مسلمانوں میں سے عادل آدمی کی گواہی لو۔ اور اللہ کے لئے گواہی قائم کرو، اس کی تم کو نصیحت کی جاتی ہے۔
Book of Testimony: Rights are accepted with the testimony of two men or one man and two women, whether the right is property or non-property, like marriage, divorce, agency, and will [2816](7). And it is accepted in childbirth, virginity, and defects. There is an athar that Umar ibn al-Khattab allowed the testimony of one man with women in marriage (a). From this athar it is understood that women's testimony is accepted in divorce, marriage, etc. Imam al-Shafi'i says: Women's testimony is accepted in property and its derivatives, not in marriage, divorce, etc. And there is an athar that Ali ibn Abi Talib said: Women's testimony is not permissible in divorce, marriage, and hudud. From this athar it is understood that women's testimony is not accepted in divorce and marriage. Therefore, they can only testify in matters of debt. [2816](7) In childbirth and virginity and women's defects where men cannot see, one woman's testimony will be accepted. When a child is born, a man cannot see women except his wife and slave-woman. Similarly, whether a woman is a virgin or not, a man cannot see that. Therefore, where a man cannot see, only women's testimony will be accepted. Similarly, for diseases of the private parts and such that a man cannot see, one woman's testimony is sufficient. And judgment will be based on it. (1) There is a hadith that the testimony of one midwife is accepted: from Hudhayfah that the Messenger of Allah allowed the testimony of the midwife (c). From this hadith it is understood that the midwife's testimony is accepted. (2) There is a hadith that a slave-woman gave testimony about nursing, and based on it the marriage was annulled. Narrated 'Uqbah ibn al-Harith that he heard him say that he married Um Yahya bint Abi Ihab, then a black slave-woman came and said: I nursed both of you. He mentioned that to the Prophet who turned away from me. He said: I moved aside, then mentioned it again. He said: How (can it be) when she claims that she nursed you both? So he forbade him from her. From this hadith, the command was given to annul the marriage based on the testimony of only one slave-woman, because in matters of nursing where men cannot see, the testimony of one woman is acceptable. (2) There is an athar: from al-Sha'bi that they said: The testimony of one woman is permissible in matters that men cannot see (b). From this athar it is understood that where men cannot see, one woman's testimony is sufficient. Imam al-Shafi'i says: In these matters, the testimony of four women is necessary. In transactions, the testimony of two men is necessary, and in testimony, for one man there are two women. Therefore, in place of two men, four women are needed for testimony to be accepted. (2) There is evidence for this in an athar: from 'Ata' ibn Abi Rabah that he said: It is not permissible except with four women in childbirth (c). From this athar it is understood that in childbirth etc., four women's testimony is required. [2817](8) And it is necessary in all of this to have 'adalah (integrity) and the wording of testimony. If the witness does not mention the wording of testimony and says 'I know' or 'I am certain', then his testimony will not be accepted. For giving testimony, two things are necessary: one is that the witness be 'adil, and the other is that the witness use the word 'ashhadu' when testifying. If instead of 'ashhadu' he says 'I know' or 'I am certain', his testimony will not be accepted. The verse emphasizes that the witness be 'adil: 'And take as witnesses two just men among you, and establish the testimony for Allah. That is instructed to you' (Surah al-Talaq 65:2). Another verse says: 'O you who have believed, testimony between you when death approaches one of you at the time of bequest'.
Source pages p. 142

Commentary
This passage is a commentary on the rules of testimony (shahada) regarding women. It begins by stating the general Hanafi ruling: in all rights (huquq), whether financial or non-financial, the testimony of two men or one man and two women is accepted. This includes marriage, divorce, agency, and will. The commentator then provides evidence from the practice of Umar ibn al-Khattab (radiAllahu anhu) who allowed testimony of one man with women in marriage. The Hanafi school considers this established practice. The passage then presents the view of Imam al-Shafi'i who restricts women's testimony to financial matters and their derivatives, excluding marriage and divorce. The commentator cites the narration from Ali ibn Abi Talib (radiAllahu anhu) that women's testimony is not allowed in divorce, marriage, and hudud. However, the Hanafi school does not follow this narration due to its weakness or because it is abrogated by the practice of Umar. Next, the passage addresses specific matters: childbirth, virginity, and defects that men cannot see. The Hanafi ruling is that one woman's testimony is sufficient in these cases because men cannot observe these matters directly. The commentator provides hadith evidence: the Prophet (sallAllahu alayhi wasallam) accepted the testimony of a midwife (qaabila) and annulled a marriage based on a slave-woman's testimony about nursing. These indicate that one woman's testimony is sufficient in matters where men cannot see. The commentator then contrasts the view of al-Shafi'i who requires four women in these matters, analogizing them to two men's testimony (since one man equals two women, so two men require four women). The Hanafi stance is that because these matters are typically known only by women, a single reliable woman's testimony is enough. Finally, the passage discusses two conditions for valid testimony: the witness must be 'adil (just, upright) and must use the explicit wording of testimony, i.e., 'ashhadu' (I testify). If the witness says 'I know' or 'I am certain' without the word of testimony, the testimony is not accepted. The commentator cites Quranic verses (Surah al-Talaq 65:2 and Surah al-Ma'ida 5:106) emphasizing the requirement of justice in witnesses and the proper establishment of testimony.

Key Terms
شهادة (shahada): Testimony given in court as evidence; the act of bearing witness.
عدالة (adalah): Integrity and uprightness of a witness; being just and reliable.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, which of the following can be proven by the testimony of one man and two women?
A) Divorce only
B) Marriage and divorce only
C) All rights including marriage, divorce, agency, and wills
D) Only financial matters

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school accepts women's testimony in all types of rights, relying on the practice of Umar, while the Shafi'i school restricts it to financial matters based on a narration from Ali.

Shahadat — Testimony
intermediate
8 min
Women's Testimony in Private Matters and Conditions of Acceptance
Ruling on women's testimony in unseen matters with inter-madhhab dispute and conditions

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain why the Hanafi school accepts the testimony of one woman in matters like childbirth and virginity, and identify the two conditions ('adalah and wording) required for any testimony to be valid.

Core Idea
In matters where men cannot see, one trustworthy woman's testimony is enough for judgment.

The passage continues with specific cases where women's testimony is particularly relevant: childbirth, virginity, and hidden defects. Because these are matters that men cannot observe directly, the Hanafi school rules that one woman's testimony is sufficient. This is supported by the hadith of the midwife and the slave-woman's testimony about nursing. The passage then outlines two universal conditions for all testimony: the witness must be 'adil (just) and must use the explicit wording 'ashhadu' (I testify). In this lesson, we explore the evidence for these rulings and the related dispute with Imam al-Shafi'i over the number of women required in such cases.

Guided Path
1
Identify the specific matters where men cannot see
Childbirth (wilada), virginity (bakara), and hidden defects like diseases of the private parts are matters that men cannot normally witness. This is the basis for a special rule.
These are called 'umur la yattali'u 'alayha al-rijal' (matters men cannot see).
2
State the Hanafi ruling: one woman suffices
In these matters, the testimony of a single woman is accepted and judgment is based on it.
This is a concession due to necessity and the fact that only women have access to such knowledge.
3
Present the Hanafi evidence from hadith
Hadith of the midwife: the Prophet accepted the testimony of a midwife. Hadith of the slave-woman: the Prophet annulled a marriage based on a slave-woman's testimony about nursing.
These show that one woman's testimony is sufficient in unseen matters.
4
Contrast with the Shafi'i position
Imam al-Shafi'i requires four women in these matters, analogizing to two men (since one man equals two women, two men equal four women).
They also cite the athar from 'Ata' requiring four women in childbirth.
5
Explain the Hanafi rebuttal and the two conditions of testimony
Hanafis argue that the hadith of the midwife and slave-woman directly contradict the analogy, and the athar from 'Ata' is not strong enough to override them. They then state two conditions for all testimony: 'adalah (justice) and the wording 'ashhadu'.
If a witness says 'I know' or 'I am certain' without 'ashhadu', the testimony is not accepted.

Book of Testimony: Rights are accepted with the testimony of two men or one man and two women, whether the right is property or non-property, like marriage, divorce, agency, and will [2816](7). And it is accepted in childbirth, virginity, and defects. There is an athar that Umar ibn al-Khattab allowed the testimony of one man with women in marriage (a). From this athar it is understood that women's testimony is accepted in divorce, marriage, etc. Imam al-Shafi'i says: Women's testimony is accepted in property and its derivatives, not in marriage, divorce, etc. And there is an athar that Ali ibn Abi Talib said: Women's testimony is not permissible in divorce, marriage, and hudud. From this athar it is understood that women's testimony is not accepted in divorce and marriage. Therefore, they can only testify in matters of debt. [2816](7) In childbirth and virginity and women's defects where men cannot see, one woman's testimony will be accepted. When a child is born, a man cannot see women except his wife and slave-woman. Similarly, whether a woman is a virgin or not, a man cannot see that. Therefore, where a man cannot see, only women's testimony will be accepted. Similarly, for diseases of the private parts and such that a man cannot see, one woman's testimony is sufficient. And judgment will be based on it. (1) There is a hadith that the testimony of one midwife is accepted: from Hudhayfah that the Messenger of Allah allowed the testimony of the midwife (c). From this hadith it is understood that the midwife's testimony is accepted. (2) There is a hadith that a slave-woman gave testimony about nursing, and based on it the marriage was annulled. Narrated 'Uqbah ibn al-Harith that he heard him say that he married Um Yahya bint Abi Ihab, then a black slave-woman came and said: I nursed both of you. He mentioned that to the Prophet who turned away from me. He said: I moved aside, then mentioned it again. He said: How (can it be) when she claims that she nursed you both? So he forbade him from her. From this hadith, the command was given to annul the marriage based on the testimony of only one slave-woman, because in matters of nursing where men cannot see, the testimony of one woman is acceptable. (2) There is an athar: from al-Sha'bi that they said: The testimony of one woman is permissible in matters that men cannot see (b). From this athar it is understood that where men cannot see, one woman's testimony is sufficient. Imam al-Shafi'i says: In these matters, the testimony of four women is necessary. In transactions, the testimony of two men is necessary, and in testimony, for one man there are two women. Therefore, in place of two men, four women are needed for testimony to be accepted. (2) There is evidence for this in an athar: from 'Ata' ibn Abi Rabah that he said: It is not permissible except with four women in childbirth (c). From this athar it is understood that in childbirth etc., four women's testimony is required. [2817](8) And it is necessary in all of this to have 'adalah (integrity) and the wording of testimony. If the witness does not mention the wording of testimony and says 'I know' or 'I am certain', then his testimony will not be accepted. For giving testimony, two things are necessary: one is that the witness be 'adil, and the other is that the witness use the word 'ashhadu' when testifying. If instead of 'ashhadu' he says 'I know' or 'I am certain', his testimony will not be accepted. The verse emphasizes that the witness be 'adil: 'And take as witnesses two just men among you, and establish the testimony for Allah. That is instructed to you' (Surah al-Talaq 65:2). Another verse says: 'O you who have believed, testimony between you when death approaches one of you at the time of bequest'.
Source pages p. 142

Commentary
This passage is a commentary on the rules of testimony (shahada) regarding women. It begins by stating the general Hanafi ruling: in all rights (huquq), whether financial or non-financial, the testimony of two men or one man and two women is accepted. This includes marriage, divorce, agency, and will. The commentator then provides evidence from the practice of Umar ibn al-Khattab (radiAllahu anhu) who allowed testimony of one man with women in marriage. The Hanafi school considers this established practice. The passage then presents the view of Imam al-Shafi'i who restricts women's testimony to financial matters and their derivatives, excluding marriage and divorce. The commentator cites the narration from Ali ibn Abi Talib (radiAllahu anhu) that women's testimony is not allowed in divorce, marriage, and hudud. However, the Hanafi school does not follow this narration due to its weakness or because it is abrogated by the practice of Umar. Next, the passage addresses specific matters: childbirth, virginity, and defects that men cannot see. The Hanafi ruling is that one woman's testimony is sufficient in these cases because men cannot observe these matters directly. The commentator provides hadith evidence: the Prophet (sallAllahu alayhi wasallam) accepted the testimony of a midwife (qaabila) and annulled a marriage based on a slave-woman's testimony about nursing. These indicate that one woman's testimony is sufficient in matters where men cannot see. The commentator then contrasts the view of al-Shafi'i who requires four women in these matters, analogizing them to two men's testimony (since one man equals two women, so two men require four women). The Hanafi stance is that because these matters are typically known only by women, a single reliable woman's testimony is enough. Finally, the passage discusses two conditions for valid testimony: the witness must be 'adil (just, upright) and must use the explicit wording of testimony, i.e., 'ashhadu' (I testify). If the witness says 'I know' or 'I am certain' without the word of testimony, the testimony is not accepted. The commentator cites Quranic verses (Surah al-Talaq 65:2 and Surah al-Ma'ida 5:106) emphasizing the requirement of justice in witnesses and the proper establishment of testimony.

Key Terms
ولادة (wilada): Childbirth; used here as a specific matter where women's testimony is accepted.
بكارة (bakara): Virginity; a matter that men cannot see directly, thus women's testimony is accepted.
عدالة (adalah): Integrity and uprightness of a witness; being just and reliable.
شهادة (shahada): Testimony given in court as evidence; the act of bearing witness.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, what is required for testimony to be accepted regarding the wording?
A) The witness must say 'I know'.
B) The witness must say 'I am certain'.
C) The witness must say 'ashhadu' (I testify).
D) No specific wording is required.

Key Takeaway
In matters where men cannot see, one woman's testimony is sufficient per Hanafi school; and all testimony requires the witness to be 'adil and to use the wording 'ashhadu'.

Testimony of a Single Woman in Matters Unseen by Men
Hanafi ruling on accepting one woman's testimony in unseen matters with proof and Shafi'i dispute

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi position on testimony of a single woman in unseen matters, cite the Prophetic hadith as proof, and compare the Shafi'i counter-argument.

Core Idea
In matters hidden from men, one woman's testimony suffices — the Hanafi school prioritizes explicit practice over analogy.

This lesson examines a specific exception to the general rule of testimony: in matters that men cannot witness, such as breastfeeding and childbirth, the Hanafi school accepts the testimony of a single woman. This ruling is derived from a clear Prophetic hadith and a Companion athar. We will explore the evidence and the Shafi'i objection based on qiyas.

Guided Path
1
Identify the exceptional matter
Pinpoint the specific cases (breastfeeding, childbirth) where the Hanafi ruling applies.
2
Examine the Hanafi proof
Analyze the hadith of the slave girl and the athar of al-Sha'bi as presented in the text.
Focus on the explicit permission of a single woman's testimony.
3
Understand the Shafi'i position
See how Imam al-Shafi'i analogizes these cases to financial transactions requiring four women.
Consider the athar of 'Ata requiring four women in childbirth.
4
Evaluate the Hanafi response
Note the refutation: the original ruling is based on necessity and Prophetic practice, not analogy.
The athar of 'Ata is not a consensus.
5
Determine the practical consequence (thamarah)
Contrast the Hanafi and Shafi'i rulings in real-life scenarios.
Hanafis accept one woman; Shafi'is require four.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
بالنساء في موضع لا يطلع عليه الرجال شهادة امرأة واحدة[۲۸۱۷](۸) (الف) ( بخاری شریف، باب شهادة الا ماء والعبید ، ص ۱۳۶۳، نمبر ۲۶۵۹ رابوداؤد شریف، باب الشهادة على الرضاع، ج ۲ ص ۱۵۱، نمبر ۳۶۰۳) اس حدیث میں صرف ایک باندی کی گواہی سے نکاح توڑنے کا حکم دیا کیونکہ دودھ پلانے پر جہاں مرد مطلع نہیں ہو سکتا ہو ایک عورت کی گواہی قابل قبول ہے (۲) اثر میں ہے۔ عن الشعبي قالوا تجوز شهادة امرأة واحدة فيما لا يطلع عليه الرجال (ب) (مصنف ابن ابى هيبة ،۸۲ ما تجوز فيه الشهادة النساء، ج رابع ، ص ۱۳۳۵، نمبر ۲۰۷۰۵ / مصنف عبدالرزاق، باب شهادة المرأة في الرضاع والنفاس ، ج ثامن ، ص ۱۳۳۳، نمبر (۱۵۴۲۳) اس اثر سے معلوم ہوا کہ جہاں مرد مطلع نہیں ہو سکتے ہوں وہاں ایک عورت کی گواہی کافی ہے۔ امام شافعی فرماتے ہیں کہ ان معاملوں میں بھی چار عورتوں کی گواہی ضروری ہے۔ معاملات میں دو مرد کی گواہی ضروری ہے۔ اور گواہی میں ایک مرد کے لئے دو عورتیں ہوتی ہیں اس لئے دومرد کے مقابلے میں چار عورتیں ہوں تب گواہی مقبول ہوگی (۲) اثر میں اس کا ثبوت ہے۔ عن عطاء بن ابي رباح قال لا يجوز الا اربع نسوة في الاستهلال (ج) (سن للبیہقی ، باب ماجاء فی عددهن ، ج عاشر، ص ۲۵۴، نمبر ۲۰۵۴۱ / مصنف عبدالرزاق، باب شهادة المرأة في الرضاع والنفاس ، ج ثامن ، ص ۱۳۳۲، نمبر ۱۵۴۲۱/ مصنف ابن ابی شیبة ، ۸۲ ما تجوز فيه شهادة النساء، ج رابع ، ص ۳۲۵ نمبر ۲۰۷۰۶) اس اثر سے معلوم ہوا کہ ولادت وغیرہ میں بھی چار عورتوں کی گواہی چاہئے ۔
For women in a place where men do not have insight, the testimony of one woman [is accepted][2817](8). (a) (Bukhari, Bab Shahadat al-Ama' wa al-'Abid, p. 1363, no. 2659; Abu Dawood, Bab al-Shahada 'ala al-Rida', vol. 2, p. 151, no. 3603) In this hadith, the command to annul the marriage was given on the testimony of a single slave girl because regarding breastfeeding, where men cannot have knowledge, the testimony of one woman is acceptable. (2) There is an athar: from al-Sha'bi, they said: The testimony of one woman is permissible in matters that men cannot see. (b) (Musannaf Ibn Abi Shayba, Bab Ma Tajuzu fihi Shahadat al-Nisa', vol. 4, p. 1335, no. 20705; Musannaf 'Abd al-Razzaq, Bab Shahadat al-Mar'a fi al-Rida' wa al-Nifas, vol. 8, p. 1333, no. 15423) From this athar, it is understood that where men cannot have knowledge, the testimony of one woman suffices. Imam al-Shafi'i says that in these matters too, the testimony of four women is necessary. In transactions, the testimony of two men is necessary, and in testimony, one man equals two women, so in place of two men, there should be four women for the testimony to be accepted. (2) There is evidence in an athar: from 'Ata ibn Abi Rabah, he said: It is not permissible except four women in matters of childbirth (istihlal). (c) (Sunan al-Bayhaqi, Bab Ma Ja'a fi 'Adadihin, vol. 10, p. 254, no. 20541; Musannaf 'Abd al-Razzaq, Bab Shahadat al-Mar'a fi al-Rida' wa al-Nifas, vol. 8, p. 1332, no. 15421; Musannaf Ibn Abi Shayba, Bab Ma Tajuzu fihi Shahadat al-Nisa', vol. 4, p. 325, no. 20706) From this athar, it is understood that in childbirth and similar matters, testimony of four women is required.
Source pages p. 143

Commentary
This passage deals with the ruling on testimony of women in situations where men cannot normally observe, such as breastfeeding, childbirth, and similar intimate matters. The Hanafi position, as stated in the matn, is that the testimony of a single woman is sufficient in such cases. This is supported by the hadith of 'Uqba ibn al-Harith, who married a woman and then a slave girl claimed she had breastfed both of them; the Prophet (peace be upon him) separated them on the testimony of this one woman. The Hanafis also cite the athar from al-Sha'bi that a single woman's testimony is accepted in matters unseen by men. In contrast, Imam al-Shafi'i holds that four women are required in these matters, analogizing to financial transactions where two men or one man and two women are needed; since two men are replaced by four women, similarly here two hypothetical men would be replaced by four women. The Hanafis respond that this analogy is not valid because the original ruling in unseen matters is based on necessity and the principle that women's testimony alone is sufficient. The athar of 'Ata requiring four women in childbirth is interpreted by Hanafis as a different view, not a binding proof. The Hanafi school maintains the position of a single woman's testimony based on the explicit practice of the Prophet and the Companions.

Key Terms
شهادة (shahada): Testimony given in court or in matters requiring legal attestation.
رضاع (rida'): Breastfeeding, a matter often unseen by men.
استهلال (istihlal): The crying of a newborn; here used to refer to childbirth.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, how many women are required to testify in matters that men cannot normally observe, such as breastfeeding?
A) Four women
B) Two women
C) One woman
D) One man and two women

Key Takeaway
In the Hanafi school, matters unseen by men are an exception: a single woman's testimony is sufficient, based on Prophetic practice and necessity.

Conditions for Valid Testimony: 'Adalah and 'Ashhadu'
Ruling that testimony requires an upright witness and the word 'ashhadu'.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the two essential conditions for a valid testimony in Hanafi fiqh and explain the Quranic proof for each.

Core Idea
No testimony without upright character and the word 'ashhadu'.

In Islamic court proceedings, testimony is a formal legal act. The Hanafi school insists on two strict conditions: the witness must be upright ('adil) and must explicitly utter the word of testimony. This lesson explores the ruling and its Quranic foundations from the matn and commentary of Al-Sharh al-Sameri.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two conditions
Read the passage carefully. The text states that in all testimony, 'adalah and the wording of shahada are necessary. List these two conditions.
The passage says 'لا بد في ذلك كله من العدالة ولفظ الشهادة'.
2
Note the consequence of omission
If the witness says 'I know' or 'I am certain' without using the word 'ashhadu', the testimony is not accepted. Understand that the word itself is a formal requirement.
The text says 'فان لم يذكر الشاهد لفظة الشهادة وقال اعلم او اتيقن لم تُقبل شهادته'.
3
Locate the Quranic proof for 'adalah
The author cites Surah al-Talaq 65:2 and Surah al-Ma'ida 5:106, both commanding that witnesses be 'dhawi 'adl'. Identify these verses and note how they establish the condition.
The verses use the phrase 'ذوا عدل' (two just people).
4
Understand the proof for the wording
The author explains that the word 'ashhadu' is required because all Quranic verses about testimony use the root sh-h-d, and the command 'wa ashhadu' implies the use of that specific wording. Also, it adds emphasis.
The commentary mentions verses like 'واستشهدوا شهيدين' and 'واشهدوا إذا تبايعتم'.
5
Summarise the Hanafi position
Combine the two conditions and their proofs into a concise ruling: testimony is accepted only if the witness is 'adil and explicitly uses the word of testimony.
This is the mufta bihi position in the Hanafi school.

(8) And necessary in all of this is 'adalah (uprightness) and the wording of shahada. So if the witness does not mention the word shahada and says 'I know' or 'I am certain', his testimony is not accepted. [2818](9) And it is necessary in all these matters to be 'adil and the word shahada. So if the witness does not mention the word shahada and says 'I know' or 'I am certain', his testimony will not be accepted. The verse emphasizes that the witness should be 'adil. The verse is: 'And call to witness two just persons among you, and establish the testimony for Allah. That is an admonition for him who believes in Allah and the Last Day.' (Surah al-Talaq 65:2) Another verse: 'O you who have believed, testimony [should be taken] among you when death approaches one of you at the time of bequest - [that of] two just men among you.' (Surah al-Ma'ida 5:106) From these two verses, it is understood that witnesses must be 'adil. The necessity of the word shahada is because it contains a kind of emphasis. Therefore, when giving testimony, the witness should use the word shahada. (2) In all verses of testimony, the word shahada is used, therefore the word shahada is also required. For this, two verses have already been mentioned. And 'And call to witness two men from among you' - in the verse 'And call to witness when you transact' (Surah al-Baqara 2:282). From these verses, it is understood that when giving testimony, the word shahada should be used. Thus, if he says 'I know' or 'I am certain', the testimony is not accepted. The definition of 'adil will come later.
Source pages p. 143

Commentary
This passage states two essential conditions for testimony: (1) the witness must be 'adil (upright, just), and (2) the testimony must be expressed using the word 'ashhadu' (I testify) or a similar explicit declaration. If the witness says 'I know' or 'I am certain' without uttering the word of testimony, it is not accepted. The proof for 'adalah comes from multiple Quranic verses: Surah al-Talaq 65:2 and Surah al-Ma'ida 5:106 command that witnesses be 'dhawi 'adl' (people of justice). The requirement of the word 'ashhadu' is derived from the fact that all Quranic verses concerning testimony use the root sh-h-d, and also because it adds emphasis. The commentary notes that the detailed definition of 'adalah will come later. This ruling ensures that testimony is a formal legal act, not a casual statement of knowledge.

Key Terms
عدالة ('adalah): Uprightness, justice; the quality of being a credible witness.
شهادة (shahada): The act of testifying; also the specific wording used.

Key Takeaway
A valid testimony requires both the witness's upright character and the explicit use of the word 'ashhadu'.

Shahadat — Testimony

Judge's Reliance on Apparent 'Adalah Except in Hudud and Qisas
Ruling with proof on judge's reliance on apparent 'adalah with exception.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on when a judge must investigate witness 'adalah and apply the rule to distinguish between hudud/qisas and other cases.

Core Idea
A Muslim's apparent 'adalah suffices in most cases; only hudud and qisas demand full scrutiny.

In Islamic legal procedure, the credibility of witnesses is fundamental. Imam Abu Hanifa (رحمه الله) established a balanced approach: the judge may rely on the outward uprightness of a Muslim witness in all matters except hudud (fixed punishments) and qisas (retaliation). This lesson examines the ruling, its textual evidence, and the rationale behind the heightened investigation in capital and severe penalty cases.

Guided Path
1
State the general rule
Identify what the judge relies on in ordinary cases: the apparent 'adalah (uprightness) of a Muslim witness.
The default is that Muslims are presumed 'adil unless proven otherwise.
2
Identify the exception
Note the exception: in hudud and qisas cases, the judge must conduct a thorough investigation into the witness's 'adalah, both open and hidden.
Hudud include crimes like zina, theft, and qadhf; qisas covers murder and injury.
3
Examine the primary dalil
Read the hadith of 'Amr ibn Shu'ayb: 'Muslims are 'udul over one another except one who has been punished for qadhf.' This establishes the presumption.
The hadith implies that only a person actually punished for false accusation loses the presumption.
4
Analyse the secondary dalil
Consider the incident of Ma'iz, where the Prophet investigated his sanity and marital status before carrying out the hadd penalty.
This demonstrates the need for caution in hudud, even when the accused confesses.
5
Understand the rationale
Reflect on why hudud and qisas require extra scrutiny: to avoid wrongful loss of life or limb, given the severity of punishments.
The principle is that it is better to err on the side of leniency in capital cases.

Source Text

[۲۸۱۸](۹) وقال ابو حنيفة رحمه الله تعالى يقتصر الحاكم على ظاهر عدالة المسلم الا فى الحدود والقصاص فانه يسأل عن الشهود وان طعن الخصم اور امام ابو حنيفہ نے فرمایا حاکم اکتفا کرے گا مسلمان کی ظاہری عدالت پر مگر حدود اور قصاص میں ۔ اس لئے کہ حدود میں تفتیش کریں گے گواہوں کے بارے میں ، اور اگر طعن کیا مدعی علیہ نے گواہوں میں تو ان کے بارے میں تفتیش کریں گے۔ امام ابو حنیفہ کی رائے یہ ہے کہ حدود اور قصاص کے علاوہ عام معاملات میں گواہوں کی عدالت کی تفتیش زیادہ نہیں کریں گے ۔ بلکہ ظاہری طور پر عادل معلوم ہوتے ہوں تو اسی پر اکتفا کریں گے اور فیصلہ کر دیا جائے گا۔ ہاں مدعی علیہ گواہوں کی عدالت پر طعن کرے تو پھر گواہوں کی تفتیش کی جائے گی۔ البتہ حدود و قصاص کے گواہوں کی پوری جانچ ہوگی۔ اور پوشیدہ اور ظاہری طور پر اس کی عدالت کی تحقیق کی جائے گی تا کہ مجرم کی جان ضائع نہ جائے یا اس کا عضو ضائع نہ جائے۔ وہ فرماتے ہیں کہ مسلمان ظاہری طور پر عادل ہیں جب تک کہ اس میں طعن نہ کرے۔ اس لئے ظاہری عدالت پر اکتفا کیا جائے گا (۲) عدیث میں ہے۔ عن عمرو بن شعيب عن ابيه عن جده قال قال رسول الله الله الله المسلمون عدول بعضهم على بعض الا محدودا في فرية (ب) (مصنف ابن ابی شیبة من من قال لا تجوز شهادته اذا تاب، ج رابع میں ۱۳۳۰، نمبر ۲۰۶۵۰ / دار قطنی کتاب عمر الی ابی موسی اشعری ، ج رابع ، ص ۱۳۲، نمبر ۴۴۲۵) اس حدیث سے معلوم ہوا کہ مسلمان عادل ہیں مگر حد قذف میں ۔ اس لئے ظاہری عدالت پر اکتفا کیا جائے گا۔ ہاں مدعی علیہ طعن کرے تو تفتیش کی جائے گی۔ حدود اور قصاص میں گواہوں کی تفتیش کی جائے گی اس کی وجہ یہ ہے ؟ جان ضائع نہ ہو (۲) حضور نے حضرت ماعر سے اس کی عدالت کے بارے میں تحقیق کی۔ حدیث کا ٹکڑا یہ ہے۔ ان ابا هريرة قال ... دعاه النبی اله الا الله فقال ایک جنون ؟ قال لا یا رسول الله! فقال احصنت ؟ قال نعم يا رسول الله ! قال اذهبوا فارجموه (ج) ( بخاری شریف، باب سوال الامام المقر هل انت ؟ ص ۱۰۰۸ نمبر ۶۸۲۵ را بود او د شریف ، باب رجم ماعز بن مالک ،ص۲۶۰، نمبر ۴۴۳۰) اس حدیث سے معلوم ہوا کہ آپ نے حدود میں عادل ہونے حاشیہ : (الف) اے ایمان والو! تمہارے درمیان گواہی یہ ہے کہ تم میں سے کسی ایک کو موت آئے وصیت کے وقت تم میں سے دو عادل آدمی ہوں۔ لعنی وصیت کے وقت عادل آدمی کی گواہی لیں (ب) آپ نے فرمایا مسلمان بعض بعض پر عادل ہیں مگر زنا کی تہمت میں جس کو مد لگ چکی ہو وہ عادل نہیں (ج) آپ نے حضرت ماعر کو بلایا اور پوچھا کیا تم کو جنون ہے؟ فرمایا نہیں یا رسول اللہ اپھر پو چھا کیا تم محصن ہو؟ کہا ہاں یا رسول اللہ ! آپ نے فرمایا جاؤ ان کو رحم کرو۔
[2818](9) And Abu Hanifa, may Allah have mercy on him, said: The judge restricts himself to the apparent 'adalah of a Muslim except in hudud and qisas, for then he asks about the witnesses, and if the opponent impugns [them]. And Imam Abu Hanifa said: The judge will be content with the apparent 'adalah of a Muslim except in hudud and qisas, because in hudud they will investigate about the witnesses, and if the defendant impugns the witnesses, then they will investigate regarding them. Imam Abu Hanifa's opinion is that in general matters other than hudud and qisas, the investigation of the witnesses' 'adalah will not be extensive. Rather, if they appear outwardly 'adil, they will be satisfied with that and a decision will be given. Yes, if the defendant impugns the witnesses' 'adalah, then investigation of the witnesses will be done. However, in hudud and qisas, there will be a full examination of the witnesses, and their 'adalah will be investigated both hidden and apparent, so that the life of the criminal is not wasted or his limb wasted. He says that Muslims are outwardly 'adil as long as they are not impugned. Therefore, reliance will be on apparent 'adalah. (2) There is a hadith: from 'Amr ibn Shu'ayb from his father from his grandfather, he said: The Messenger of Allah said: 'Muslims are 'udul (just) over one another except one who has been punished for qadhf (false accusation of zina).' (Musannaf Ibn Abi Shayba, Bab Man Qala La Tajuzu Shahadatuhu Idha Taba, vol. 4, p. 1330, no. 20650; Dar Qutni, Kitab 'Umar ila Abi Musa al-Ash'ari, vol. 4, p. 132, no. 4425) From this hadith, it is understood that Muslims are 'adil except one who has been given the hadd penalty for qadhf. Therefore, reliance will be on apparent 'adalah. Yes, if the defendant impugns, investigation will be done. In hudud and qisas, investigation of witnesses will be done because lives may be lost. (2) The Prophet investigated about the 'adalah of Ma'iz. The hadith fragment: That Abu Huraira said... The Prophet called him and said: 'Is there madness?' He said: 'No, O Messenger of Allah.' Then he said: 'Are you muhsan?' He said: 'Yes, O Messenger of Allah.' He said: 'Go and stone him.' (Bukhari, Bab Su'al al-Imam al-Muqirr Hal Anta, p. 1008, no. 6825; Abu Dawood, Bab Rajm Ma'iz ibn Malik, p. 260, no. 4430) From this hadith, it is understood that in hudud, he investigated 'adalah.
Source pages p. 144

Commentary
This passage presents the ruling of Imam Abu Hanifa regarding the judge's assessment of witness 'adalah. According to Abu Hanifa, in all cases except hudud (fixed punishments) and qisas (retaliation), the judge may rely on the apparent 'adalah of a Muslim witness. Muslims are presumed to be righteous outwardly, based on the hadith 'Muslims are 'udul over one another except the one punished for qadhf.' Therefore, unless the defendant (khasm) impugns the witness's character, no further investigation is needed. However, in hudud and qisas cases, the judge must conduct a thorough investigation into the witness's 'adalah, both open and hidden, because these cases involve severe penalties such as loss of life or limb. This strictness is to avoid any miscarriage of justice. The commentator also cites the incident of Ma'iz where the Prophet inquired about his sanity and marital status before carrying out the hadd penalty, demonstrating the need for caution in hudud. The overall principle is that the default is trust in a Muslim's apparent uprightness until proven otherwise.

Key Terms
ظاهر العدالة (zahir al-'adala): Apparent uprightness; the outward appearance of being a righteous Muslim.
حدود (hudud): Fixed punishments for certain crimes prescribed in the Quran or Sunnah.
قصاص (qisas): Retaliation for murder or injury, where the victim's family can demand execution or blood money.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Imam Abu Hanifa, in which types of cases must the judge conduct a thorough investigation into the witnesses' 'adalah?
A) All civil cases
B) Only hudud cases
C) Both hudud and qisas cases
D) Only when the defendant is a non-Muslim

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi law, the judge presumes a Muslim witness's 'adalah except in hudud and qisas, where rigorous investigation is mandatory to avoid severe miscarriages of justice.

Requirement of Justice and Specific Wording in Testimony
Ruling on witness justice and required wording 'ashhadu'

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the two conditions for valid testimony in Hanafi fiqh and apply the ruling that testimony must be given with the word 'ashhadu' by a just witness.

Core Idea
Testimony requires a just witness and the explicit wording 'ashhadu'—derived directly from the Quran.

Testimony is a serious act that can determine life, property, and honor. The Hanafi school, drawing from the Quran, sets two clear conditions for its validity: the witness must be upright in character ('adil) and must utter the specific word 'ashhadu' (I testify). This lesson unpacks these conditions, their Quranic proof, and a legitimate scholarly difference on the wording requirement.

Guided Path
1
Identify the conditions for valid testimony
From the passage, note the two conditions: the witness must be just ('adil) and must use the word 'ashhadu'. The passage explicitly rejects 'a'lamu' (I know) or 'atiqanu' (I am certain).
2
Locate the Quranic dalil
The passage cites Quran 5:106 ('two just men from among you') and 2:282 ('and call two witnesses from among your men'). Identify that the word 'shahada' appears in these verses, implying the required wording.
The imperative 'istashhidu' indicates obligation in Hanafi usul.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
The Quranic command to 'bring witnesses' (istashhidu) and the use of the word 'shahada' indicate that testimony must be verbally expressed with that specific term. The Hanafi principle is that the imperative implies obligation (wujub).
Thus saying 'ashhadu' is wajib, and omission invalidates the testimony.
4
Note the cross-madhhab difference
Some schools (e.g., Shafi'i) accept synonyms like 'a'lamu' if they convey certainty. The Hanafi school insists on 'ashhadu' because the Quran consistently uses the root sh-h-d for testimony.
This is a valid ikhtilaf; the Hanafi position is mufta bihi.
5
Apply the ruling
Given a scenario, check both conditions: Is the witness 'adil? Did they say 'ashhadu'? If both are met, testimony is accepted; otherwise it is rejected.
In hudud and qisas cases, the judge must actively investigate 'adalah.

اثنان ذوا عدل منكم (الف) ( آیت ۱۰۶، سورۃ المائدة (۵) ان دونوں آیتوں سے معلوم ہوا کہ گواہ عادل ہوں۔ لفظ شہادت کی ضرورت اس لئے ہے کہ اس میں ایک قسم کی تاکید ہے۔ اس لئے گواہ گواہی دیتے وقت شہادت کا لفظ استعمال کرے (۲) گوہی کی تمام آیتوں میں شہادت کا لفظ استعمال ہوا ہے اس لئے بھی شہادت کا لفظ چاہئے ۔ اس کے لئے دو آیتیں تو پہلے گزر گئیں۔ اور استشهدوا شهيدين من رجالكم ، ای آیت میں ہے واشهدوا اذا تبا يعتم (آیت ۲۸۲) سورة البقرة ۲) ان آیتوں سے معلوم ہوا کہ گواہی دیتے وقت لفظ شہادت استعمال کرے۔ چنانچہ اعلم یا اتیقن کہے تو گواہی مقبول نہیں ہوگی۔ عادل کس کو کہتے ہیں اس کی تفصیل آگے آئے گی۔
If he says 'I am certain' his testimony is not accepted. (2818)(9) And Abu Hanifa, may Allah have mercy on him, said: The judge relies on the apparent justice of a Muslim except in Hudud and Qisas, for then he asks about the witnesses even if the opponent challenges. "Two just men from among you" (Quran 5:106). From these two verses it is understood that witnesses must be just. The word 'shahada' is needed because it contains a type of emphasis. Therefore the witness should use the word 'shahada' when testifying. (2) In all verses of testimony, the word 'shahada' is used, so the word 'shahada' is required. There are two verses that have passed earlier. And 'and call two witnesses from among your men' (Quran 2:282) and 'and call witnesses when you transact' (Quran 2:282). From these verses it is understood that when testifying the word 'shahada' should be used. Thus if he says 'I know' or 'I am certain', the testimony is not accepted. Who is just? Commentary
This passage is a ruling with textual proof. It establishes two requirements for valid testimony: (1) the witness must be 'adil (just), based on Quran 5:106; (2) the witness must explicitly use the word 'ashhadu' (I testify) rather than 'a'lamu' (I know) or 'atiqanu' (I am certain). This is derived from the Quranic usage of the word shahada in all testimony verses, implying a specific verbal formulation. The passage then introduces Abu Hanifa's position on investigating 'adalah: in general cases, the judge accepts the apparent justice of a Muslim witness, but in Hudud and Qisas cases, he must investigate the witnesses even without a challenge. The hadith of the Prophet (saw) that 'Muslims are just to one another except for one who has been flogged for slander' supports relying on apparent 'adalah. The passage concludes that the details of what constitutes 'adalah will follow later.

Key Terms
شهادت (shahādat): Testimony given in court using the specific wording 'ashhadu'.
عدل ('adl): Justice; a witness must be a Muslim of upright character who avoids major sins and maintains good conduct.
حدود (ḥudūd): Fixed punishments for crimes like theft and fornication; in these cases the judge must investigate 'adalah actively.

Key Takeaway
For a testimony to be accepted in Hanafi fiqh, the witness must be 'adil and must explicitly say 'ashhadu'.

Dispute on Investigating Witnesses' 'Adalah
Intra-Hanafi dispute on secret and public investigation of witnesses

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the two Hanafi positions on tazkiyah of witnesses, identify the mufta bihi, and explain the justification based on changing social circumstances.

Core Idea
The Hanafi ruling on witness investigation changed from relying on apparent justice to mandatory inquiry as social trust declined.

This lesson examines an intra-Hanafi dispute that illustrates how fiqh adapts to changing social conditions. Imam Abu Hanifa held that in most cases, a Muslim's apparent 'adalah is sufficient unless challenged. His two students, Abu Yusuf and Muhammad, argued that judges must actively investigate witnesses secretly and publicly in all cases. The author of al-Hidayah explains that the difference is not a contradiction but a response to moral decline: the Sahibayn's view became the operative fatwa.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two positions
State Imam Abu Hanifa's view: the judge relies on the apparent 'adalah of a Muslim except in Hudud and Qisas, where investigation is required even without a challenge. State the Sahibayn's view: investigation (tazkiyah) is necessary in all cases, both secretly and publicly.
Note that Abu Hanifa also allows investigation if the opponent challenges.
2
Analyze the proofs
For Abu Hanifa: the hadith 'Muslims are just to one another except for one flogged for slander' and the fact that the Prophet did not routinely investigate witnesses. For the Sahibayn: the Prophet investigated Ma'iz's sanity and 'Umar's investigation of Abu Jumayla's background.
The Sahibayn argue that 'adalah is a condition for testimony and must be verified.
3
Understand the tarjih mechanism
The author of al-Hidayah reconciles the positions by noting the moral decline over time. In Abu Hanifa's era, people were generally upright; in later times, they became less reliable. Thus, the Sahibayn's view became the mufta bihi.
This shows that tarjih can be based on changing social realities, not just textual strength.
4
Apply the mufta bihi
In contemporary practice, a judge must actively investigate the 'adalah of witnesses in all cases, regardless of whether the opponent challenges, and even if the witnesses appear Muslim and upright.
This has practical implications for court procedures and the burden of proof.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
[۲۸۱۸](۹) وقال ابو حنيفة رحمه الله تعالى يقتصر الحاكم على ظاهر عدالة المسلم الا فى الحدود والقصاص فانه يسأل عن الشهود وان طعن الخصم ... و قال ابو حنيفة رحمه الله تعالى يقتصر الحاكم على ظاهر عدالة المسلم الا فى الحدود والقصاص فانه يسأل عن الشهود وان طعن الخصم ... وقال ابو يوسف و محمد رحمهما الله تعالى لا بد ان يسأل عنهم في السر والعلانية [۱۲۸۲۰ (۱۰) ... و صاحب هدایة نے فرمایا کہ حضرت امام ابو حنیفہ کے زمانے میں لوگ اچھے ہوتے تھے اس لئے عام معاملات میں گواہوں کے تزکیہ کی ضرورت نہیں سمجھی ۔ اور صاحبین کے زمانے میں لوگ کچھ غیر ذمہ دار ہو گئے تھے اس لئے تزکیہ کی ضرورت سمجھی گئی۔ اور اس وقت انہیں کے قول پر فتوی ہے۔
(2818)(9) Abu Hanifa, may Allah have mercy on him, said: The judge relies on the apparent justice of the Muslim except in Hudud and Qisas, for he asks about the witnesses even if the opponent challenges. ... Abu Yusuf and Muhammad, may Allah have mercy on them, said: It is necessary to ask about them secretly and publicly. [12820](10)... And the author of al-Hidayah said: In the time of Imam Abu Hanifa, people were good, so there was no need for tazkiyah of witnesses in general cases. In the time of the Sahibayn, people became somewhat irresponsible, so tazkiyah became necessary. And in our time, the fatwa is on their (Sahibayn's) statement.
Source pages p. 144

Commentary
This passage presents an intra-Hanafi dispute between Imam Abu Hanifa and his two students, Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani, regarding the investigation of witnesses' 'adalah. Abu Hanifa holds that in cases other than Hudud and Qisas, the judge may rely on the apparent 'adalah of a Muslim witness. Only if the opponent challenges the witness's 'adalah does the judge investigate. In Hudud and Qisas, however, investigation is always required due to the gravity of the punishments. The Sahibayn hold that investigation (tazkiyah) is necessary in all cases, both secretly and publicly, because 'adalah is a condition for testimony and people's conditions are not always apparent. They support this with the hadith of the Prophet investigating Ma'iz's sanity and the story of Abu Jumayla foundling. The author of al-Hidayah reconciles the positions by noting the change in times: in Abu Hanifa's era, people were generally upright, so investigation was unnecessary; in later times, due to moral decline, the Sahibayn's view became the operative one. Thus, the mufta bihi (relied-upon position) is that of the Sahibayn.

Key Terms
تزكية (tazkiyah): Investigation and verification of a witness's 'adalah (justice).
ظاهر عدالة (zāhir 'adālah): Apparent justice; a Muslim is presumed just unless proven otherwise.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) Imam Abu Hanifa
B) Imam Abu Yusuf
C) Imam Muhammad al-Shaybani
D) Both Sahibayn

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school's mufta bihi on witness investigation requires active verification in all cases, reflecting the principle that fiqh adapts to changing social realities.
