The First Type of Testimony Bearing: Direct Observation
Definition of two categories of testimonial bearing

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish the two categories of testimony bearing and state the conditions for valid testimony based on direct observation.

Core Idea
Testimony based on direct sensory observation does not require formal appointment — knowledge alone permits bearing witness.

This passage from the Hanafi fiqh text clarifies a fundamental distinction in the law of testimony (shahadah). It introduces two categories of bearing testimony (tahammul al-shahadah) and details the first: acts whose legal significance is established by the act itself, independent of any formal appointment. Understanding this distinction is crucial for correctly executing the witness's role in Islamic courts.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two categories
The passage states that testimony bearing is of two types. Read the opening line to identify both categories. Note that only the first is fully described; the second is implied but not elaborated here.
The two categories are: (1) where the ruling is established by the act itself, and (2) where the ruling is established by appointment (muqaddar).
2
Recognize examples of the first type
The passage lists examples: sale, acknowledgment, usurpation, and a judge's judgment. These are acts that can be directly observed or heard. Understand why each fits the first category—they exist independently of any witness designation.
These examples involve contracts, torts, and judicial acts—all produce legal effects upon occurrence.
3
Determine the condition for validity
The witness must have directly heard or seen the act. This sensory perception is the basis for knowledge and the key condition for testimony under this category.
Secondhand knowledge (hearsay) does not suffice for this type.
4
Extract the required phrasing
The witness should phrase the testimony as 'I testify that he sold' not 'I was made a witness.' This phrasing reflects direct knowledge and avoids implying formal appointment.
The correct wording preserves the nature of the testimony as based on personal observation.
5
Understand the legal implication
The testimony is valid even if the witness was not appointed. This allows spontaneous witnesses to come forward and fulfill their duty without prior designation.
This principle encourages the disclosure of truth even without formal procedures.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
(۱۲۸۲۰ (۱۱) گواہ جس گواہی کا تحمل کرتا ہے اس کی دوقسمیں ہیں۔ ان میں سے ایک وہ جس کا حکم ثابت ہوتا ہے خود ہی۔ جیسے خریدو فروخت، اقرار ، غصب قبل، حاکم کا فیصلہ، پس گواہ چیزوں کو سنے یا ان کو دیکھے تو اس کے لئے گنجائش ہے کہ ان کی گواہی دے۔ چاہے ان پر گواہ نہ بنایا ہو۔ اور یوں کہے کہ میں گواہی دیتا ہوں کہ اس نے بیچا ہے۔ یوں نہ کہے کہ مجھ کو گواہ بنایا ہے۔
(12820)(11) The testimony that a witness bears is of two types. One is that whose ruling is established by itself, such as sale, acknowledgment, usurpation, judgment of a judge. So if the witness hears these things or sees them, it is permissible for him to testify about them, even if he was not appointed as a witness over them. And he should say: I testify that he sold. He should not say: I was made a witness.
Source pages p. 145

Commentary
This passage defines two categories of testimony a witness may bear. The first type is testimony about acts whose legal rulings are established by the act itself, not by the appointment of the witness. Examples include sales, acknowledgments, usurpations, and judicial decisions. In such cases, the witness's knowledge comes from direct sensory perception (seeing or hearing). The witness does not need to have been formally appointed; it is sufficient that he witnessed the event. When testifying, he must use the phrasing that reflects his direct knowledge (e.g., 'I testify that he sold'), not that he was appointed as a witness. This distinction matters because the legal validity of the testimony depends on the nature of the witness's knowledge.

Key Terms
تحمل شهادة (taḥammul al-shahādah): The act of receiving and bearing testimony; the process by which a witness comes to know the subject of testimony.
حکم ثابت خود ہی (ḥukm thābit khud hī): Ruling that is established by the act itself, independent of appointment.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, which of the following is an example of the first type of testimony bearing?
A) Sale
B) Appointment to a will
C) Written contract
D) Judge's order that required witnesses

Key Takeaway
Direct observation of an act suffices for bearing testimony without formal appointment; the witness's phrasing must reflect direct knowledge, not appointment.

Investigating Witnesses in Private and Public
Intra-Hanafi dispute on tazkiyah procedure

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the dispute between Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn regarding the necessity of secret and open tazkiyah of witnesses, and identify the mufta bihi position.

Core Idea
The Hanafi mufta bihi requires tazkiyah of witnesses in all cases, not just hudud, due to changed times.

In this passage, a key intra-Hanafi dispute is examined: should judges investigate witnesses secretly and openly in all cases or only in hudud and qisas? The Sahibayn argued for general application, while Imam Abu Hanifa limited it to severe punishments. Understanding this dispute reveals how Hanafi fiqh adapts to changing social conditions.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two positions
State the view of Imam Abu Hanifa (tazkiyah only in hudud and qisas) and the view of Abu Yusuf and Muhammad (tazkiyah in all cases).
Both are within the Hanafi school.
2
Examine the evidence for each
Note the dalil: Sahibayn cite the Prophet's investigation in the hadith of Ma'iz and Aisha, and Umar's investigation of the foundling. Abu Hanifa relied on general trustworthiness of people in his time.
The evidence is from sunnah and athar.
3
Understand the tarjih mechanism
Al-Marghinani in Al-Hidayah explains that the ruling changed because times changed (taghayyur al-ahkam bi taghayyur al-zaman), making Sahibayn's view mufta bihi.
This is a key principle in Hanafi Iftaa.
4
Apply the mufta bihi to a modern scenario
In a modern court, a judge must investigate all witnesses, even in civil cases, to ensure their 'adalah.
Practical consequence: tazkiyah is wajib in all cases.

Concerning them, he asked about them (10) Abu Yusuf and Muhammad (may Allah have mercy on them) said: It is necessary to ask about them in secret and openly. (1) And what the witness bears is of two types: one of them... (explanation in Urdu). A hadith: from Ibn Abbas... he turned away from him and asked his people: Is he mad? They said: There is no harm. (al-footnote) This hadith shows that in hudud and qisas, tazkiyah should be done secretly and openly. (10) Imam Abu Yusuf and Imam Muhammad say: It is necessary to investigate witnesses in secret and openly. The Sahibayn hold that in common transactions also the court should investigate witnesses in secret and openly. They say: In transactions, the condition of testimony is justice ('adalah), and in this time it is difficult to know justice without investigation, so he should investigate. (2) The Prophet also investigated regarding Aisha. A piece of the long hadith of Ifk: from Aisha... He said: O Zainab, what do you know and what have you seen? She said: O Messenger of Allah, Allah protects my hearing and sight; by Allah, I know only good of her. (b) (Bukhari). (3) There is an athar: Abu Jamilah said: I found an abandoned child. When Umar saw me, he said: 'Asa al-ghuwair abusa (i.e., it seems the poor one has become poor), as if he suspected me. My chief said: He is a righteous man. He said: So it is; go, his maintenance is upon me. (c) (Bukhari). This hadith and athar show tazkiyah and investigation in common matters. Therefore, he should investigate witnesses even in common matters. And the author of Hidayah said: In the time of Imam Abu Hanifa, people were good, so he did not consider it necessary to investigate witnesses in common matters. In the time of the Sahibayn, people became somewhat irresponsible, so they considered investigation necessary. And now the fatwa is on their opinion.
Source pages p. 145

Commentary
This passage is an intra-Hanafi dispute regarding the necessity of tazkiyah (investigation of witnesses' credibility) in both secret and open manners. The Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) argue that for all cases, including civil transactions, the judge must inquire about witnesses privately and publicly. They support this with the Prophet's investigation in the cases of Ma'iz and Aisha, and Umar's investigation of Abu Jamilah. Imam Abu Hanifa held that such investigation is only required for hudud and qisas, not for common transactions because the people of his time were generally trustworthy. However, the later reliance (mufta bihi) is on the Sahibayn due to changed times. The commentary explains the practical consequence: today, judges should always investigate witnesses.

Key Terms
تزکیہ (tazkiyah): Investigation into the credibility and moral integrity of witnesses.
سر (sirr): Secret or private investigation, not in the presence of the litigants.
علانیہ (alāniyah): Open or public investigation, in the presence of the parties.

Key Terms from Source Passage

B) Only in financial transactions

D) Only if the witness is suspect

Key Takeaway
The relied-upon Hanafi position requires judges to investigate all witnesses secretly and openly to ensure justice in all types of cases.

Two Types of Testimony in Hanafi Fiqh
Definition and conditions for direct and secondary testimony

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish between self-proving testimony and testimony on testimony, and state the condition required for secondary testimony in the Hanafi school.

Core Idea
Direct testimony is binding without formal appointment; secondary testimony requires formal constitution by the original witness.

In this passage from a Hanafi manual, the author categorises testimony into two types: those where the act itself is witnessed (self-proving), and those where the testimony is based on another witness's statement. Understanding this distinction is essential for knowing when you can testify directly and when you need to have been formally appointed as a secondary witness.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two categories
The passage begins: 'ما يتحمله الشاهد على ضربين' – what the witness bears is of two types. List the two: (1) self-proving matters, and (2) testimony on testimony.
Self-proving matters include sale, confession, usurpation, killing, and the judge's ruling.
2
Analyze the first type: self-proving
For self-proving matters, the witness directly sees or hears the act. He can testify without being formally appointed. He states: 'اشهد انه باع' – I testify that he sold.
No phrase like 'اشهدنی' is needed.
3
Analyze the second type: testimony on testimony
For secondary testimony, the subsidiary witness conveys the original witness's testimony. This is only permissible if the original witness explicitly made him a witness, e.g., by saying 'اشهدنی'.
If he only hears the original testify, he cannot testify on it.
4
Understand the reason for the restriction
The passage warns of 'الورطة' (danger) because the subsidiary bears testimony from an untrustworthy source (غير ثقة). Hearsay is inherently unreliable.
This protects the integrity of the judiciary.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وما يتحمله الشاهد على ضربين احدهما ما يثبت حكمه بنفسه مثل البيع والاقرار والغصب والقتل وحكم الحاكم فاذا سمع ذلك الشاهد او راه وسعه ان يشهد به وان لم يشهد عليه ويقول اشهد انه باع ولا يقول اشهدنی [۲۸۲۱ (۱۲) ومنه ما لا يثبت حكمه بنفسه مثل الشهادة على الشهادة فاذا سمع شاهدا يشهد بشيء لم يجز له ان يشهد على شهادته الا ان يُشهده وكذلك لو سمع انه يُشهد على شهادة لم يسعه ان يشهد على ذلك لما فيه من الورطة لانه يتحملها عن غير ثقة وقد وصله من طريق مستور
And what the witness bears is of two types: one of them is that which its ruling is established by itself, such as sale, confession, usurpation, killing, and the judge's ruling. So if that witness hears or sees it, it is permissible for him to testify to it even if he was not made a witness upon it, and he says, 'I testify that he sold,' and he does not say, 'He made me a witness.' And from it is that which its ruling is not established by itself, such as testimony upon testimony. So if he hears a witness testifying to something, it is not permissible for him to testify to his testimony unless he (the original) made him a witness. Similarly, if he hears that he is being made a witness upon a testimony, it is not permissible for him to testify to that because of the danger involved, since he bears it from someone not trustworthy, and it reaches him through a concealed path.
Source pages p. 145

Commentary
This passage defines two categories of testimony. The first category includes matters that are self-proving, i.e., the act itself (sale, confession, etc.) is witnessed directly. Such testimony does not require the witness to have been formally constituted; it suffices that he saw or heard the event. He should phrase his testimony by stating the fact, not by saying 'he made me a witness.' The second category is testimony on testimony (shahadat 'ala al-shahadah), where a person wants to convey the testimony of another to the court. This is only permissible if the original witness formally appointed him as a witness to his testimony. If someone merely hears another testifying or is told about it, he cannot testify on that unless he was properly constituted. The reason is that the subsidiary witness bears responsibility for conveying the testimony, and it must be from a trustworthy source; random hearsay is not acceptable due to the risk of error.

Key Terms
شهادة على الشهادة (shahādat 'alā al-shahādah): Testimony given by a subsidiary witness about the testimony of an original witness.
تحمل الشهادة (taḥammul al-shahādah): The process of bearing or undertaking testimony, i.e., the witness's reception of knowledge of the event.
اشهدنی (ashhadanī): He made me a witness (used for constitution for secondary testimony).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) No, because he was not made a witness
B) Yes, because the act is self-proving
C) Yes, but he must say 'he made me a witness'
D) No, because he must have been present at the contract

Key Takeaway
Testimony on testimony is only valid if the original witness formally constituted the subsidiary witness; otherwise it is impermissible due to risk of unreliability.

Shahadat — Testimony

Testimony upon Testimony: The Requirement of Explicit Appointment
Explains two categories of testimony and condition for secondary testimony

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish between direct testimony and testimony upon testimony, and apply the Hanafi condition that secondary testimony requires formal appointment by the original witness.

Core Idea
Secondary testimony is only valid if the original witness formally appoints the secondary witness — knowledge by hearing is not enough.

This passage from the Book of Testimonies introduces a key classification. Some matters like sales or acknowledgments can be testified to by anyone who directly witnessed them. But testimony upon testimony — where a secondary witness relays the original witness's statement — follows a different rule: explicit appointment is required. We will examine the proof from hadith and the rationale behind this Hanafi position.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two categories
Read the passage to find the two types: (1) matters whose legal effect is established by themselves (e.g., sale, acknowledgment) — direct testimony allowed without appointment; (2) matters that require appointment, specifically testimony upon testimony.
The term 'yuthbitu hukmahu bi nafsihi' refers to acts that are legally self-evident.
2
Locate the condition for secondary testimony
The passage states: 'لا يجز له ان يشهد على شهادته الا ان يُشهده' — it is not permissible for him to testify on his testimony unless he (the original) makes him a witness. This is the core rule.
The verb 'yushhiduhu' means to formally make someone a witness.
3
Examine the proof (hadith)
The hadith from Ibn Abbas commands not to testify until the matter is as clear as the sun. In Hanafi usul, the imperative indicates wujub of certainty. This supports the strict requirement for appointment in secondary testimony, ensuring certainty is preserved.
The hadith is ahad (zanni al-thubut) but its meaning is relied upon.
4
Understand the agency analogy
The commentary says the secondary witness is like a wakil (agent) of the original. Without appointment, the agency is invalid. Thus, the secondary witness cannot act without explicit authorization.
This analogy ties the rule to the broader principle of agency in Hanafi fiqh.
5
Apply the rule to a scenario
Consider a case: Zaid hears Amr testifying in a gathering that he saw a contract. Zaid later wants to testify in court based on Amr's testimony. According to this lesson, Zaid cannot do so unless Amr formally appointed him as a secondary witness.
This highlights the practical consequence of the rule.

حاشیہ : (الف) جو اللہ کے علاوہ کسی کو پکارتے ہیں وہ شفاعت کے لائق نہیں ہے۔ مگر جو حق کی گواہی دے اور جانتا ہو ( ب ) حضور کے سامنے ایک آدمی کا تذکرہ ہوا کہ وہ گواہی دیتا ہے۔ تو آپ نے فرمایا اے ابن عباس ! تم کسی معاملے پر اس وقت تک گواہی نہ دینا جب اس سورج کی روشنی کی طرح واضح نہ ہو جائے۔ اور حضور نے اپنے ہاتھ سے سورج کی طرف اشارہ فرمایا۔
Book of Testimonies. That whose ruling is established by itself, such as sale, acknowledgment, usurpation, killing, and the judge's ruling. So when that witness hears or sees it, it is permissible for him to testify to it even if he was not made a witness, and he says: 'I testify that he sold' and does not say 'He made me a witness.' [2821] (12) And from it is that whose ruling is not established by itself, such as testimony upon testimony. So if he hears a witness testifying to something, it is not permissible for him to testify to his testimony unless he [the original witness] makes him a witness. Likewise, if you go and present my testimony, this is called testimony upon testimony. The second case is that someone did not make him a witness, but he saw an action taking place, so he automatically became a witness. Now he has the latitude to give testimony on that matter. Now he is the original witness. For example, if he saw someone selling something, he can testify: 'So-and-so sold such-and-such to so-and-so. I give testimony on it.' However, he should not say: 'He made me a witness.' Because in reality, no one made him a witness; rather, he automatically became one. Reference to the verse: 'And those they invoke besides Him do not possess intercession except those who bear witness to the truth while they know.' (Surah al-Zukhruf 43:86) This verse indicates that one who sees and knows the truth owns intercession. (2) A hadith: From Ibn Abbas: The Messenger of Allah, peace be upon him, was mentioned a man who gives testimony. He said: 'As for you, O Ibn Abbas, do not testify except on a matter that is clear to you like the brightness of this sun.' And the Messenger of Allah pointed with his hand to the sun. (Sunan al-Bayhaqi, Chapter on Caution in Testimony and Knowledge of It, vol. 10, p. 263, no. 20579) From this hadith it is understood that when a matter becomes as clear as the sun, he can testify. [2821] (12) Among them is testimony whose ruling is not established by itself, such as testimony upon testimony. So if someone hears a witness testifying to something, it is not permissible for him to testify on his testimony unless he makes him a witness. Similarly, if he hears that he is making him a witness on someone's testimony, then the hearer does not have the latitude to testify on it. To become a witness on a witness's testimony, it is necessary that the original witness makes the secondary witness a witness on his testimony. Then he can transfer his testimony to the judge's court; without that, not. So if he hears someone making him a witness, the hearer does not have latitude to testify in the judge's court. Or if he sees someone giving testimony, the observer does not have latitude to transfer his testimony to the judge's court until the original witness formally makes the secondary witness a witness on his testimony. The secondary witness is like an agent of the original witness, and without the principal's appointment, he does not become an agent; therefore, without the original witness, the secondary witness cannot become a witness. (2) Footnote: (a) Those who call upon other than Allah are not worthy of intercession, except those who bear witness to the truth and know. (b) A man was mentioned in the presence of the Prophet that he gives testimony. The Prophet said: 'O Ibn Abbas! Do not testify on a matter until it becomes as clear as the light of this sun.' And the Prophet pointed to the sun with his hand.
Source pages p. 146

Commentary
This passage from the Book of Testimonies introduces a fundamental classification: matters whose legal effect is established by the act itself (like a sale or acknowledgment) versus those that require specific appointment for testimony. In the first category, a witness who directly sees or hears such an act may testify in court without being formally appointed; his knowledge is sufficient. The second category is testimony upon testimony (shahada ala al-shahada), where the secondary witness must be explicitly appointed by the original witness to relay the testimony. The passage supports this with the Quranic verse indicating that testimony must be based on certain knowledge, and the hadith requiring clarity like the sun. The Urdu commentary elaborates: hearing or seeing a witness testify does not automatically make one a secondary witness; the original witness must formally designate him. This is analogized to agency (wakala): the secondary witness acts as an agent and cannot testify without the principal's authorization.

Key Terms
الشهادة (al-shahada): Testimony given in court regarding a legal right or fact.
الشهادة على الشهادة (al-shahada ala al-shahada): Testimony given by a secondary witness who relays the testimony of the original witness.
الشاهد الأصلي (al-shahid al-asli): The original witness who directly observed the event.
الشاهد الفرعي (al-shahid al-far'i): The secondary witness who testifies on behalf of the original witness.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, what is required for a secondary witness to give testimony on testimony?
A) The secondary witness must have seen the original event.
B) The original witness must explicitly appoint the secondary witness.
C) The secondary witness must be a relative of the original witness.
D) The second witness must be present when the original witness testifies in court.

Key Takeaway
Testimony upon testimony requires explicit appointment by the original witness; mere hearing or seeing is insufficient.

Shahadat — Testimony

Testifying Based on Handwriting Without Memory
Ruling with proof from a tabi'i report

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on testifying based solely on handwriting and apply the condition that memory of the testimony is required.

Core Idea
Handwriting alone is not certainty; testimony requires independent memory of the event.

This lesson addresses a common scenario: a witness finds a document in his own handwriting containing a testimony, but does not recall the event. The Hanafi school holds that the witness cannot testify based solely on the handwriting. We will explore the proof and the underlying principle of certainty (yaqin) required for testimony.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and ruling
The act is testifying based on one's own handwriting without independently remembering the content of the testimony. The ruling is that it is unlawful (haram) to testify in such a case.
The text uses 'la yahillu' (not permissible), indicating prohibition.
2
Locate the dalil
The passage cites the report (athar) from al-Sha'bi, a tabi'i, who said: 'Do not testify until you remember.' This is a qawl sahabi (statement of a Companion-level scholar) and serves as the proof.
The full report is in Musannaf Abd al-Razzaq and Sunan al-Bayhaqi.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
The imperative 'la tashhad' (do not testify) indicates prohibition. The reason (illah) is that handwriting resembles handwriting and may be forged; therefore, it does not produce certainty (yaqin). Testimony requires yaqin.
The Hanafi principle: testimony must be based on certain knowledge, not conjecture.
4
Note intra-Hanafi agreement
There is no disagreement within the Hanafi school on this point. All three imams (Abu Hanifa, Abu Yusuf, Muhammad al-Shaybani) hold that memory is required.
This is from the zahir al-riwayah.
5
Apply to a scenario
A witness sees a document in his handwriting that records a loan agreement, but he does not recall the loan. He cannot testify in court based solely on the document. If the memory returns, he may testify.
The condition is independent recall of the event, not recognition of handwriting.

تشریح شہادت شاہد سے مشتق ہے یعنی دیکھ کر گواہی دینا اس لئے جن باتوں میں دیکھ کر گواہی دینا ہوتا ہے اس میں نابینا کی گواہی مقبول نہیں ہے۔ البتہ جن باتوں میں صرف سن کر گواہی دینا ہوتا ہے ان میں امام ابو یوسف کی رائے یہ ہے کہ نابینا کی گواہی مقبول ہے۔ اثر میں ہے۔ حدثنا الاسود بن قيس العنزى سمع قومه يقولون ان عليا رد شهادة اعمى في سرقة لم يجزها (ج) (سنن للبیہقی ، باب وجوه العلم بالشهادة ، ج عاشر ص ۲۶۶، نمبر ۲۰۵۸۶ / مصنف عبد الرزاق، باب شهادة الاعمی ، ج ثامن ، ص ۳۲۴، نمبر ۱۵۳۸۰) اس اثر سے معلوم ہوا کہ نابینا کی گواہی مقبول نہیں ہے (۳) حدیث میں ہے کہ سورج کی طرح روشن ہو جائے تب گواہی دو اور نا بینا دیکھ نہیں سکتا اس لئے اس کے سامنے سورج کی طرح روشن نہیں ہوگا۔ اس لئے وہ گواہی بھی نہیں دے سکتا۔ حدیث یہ ہے۔ عن ابن عباس
حاشیہ : (الف) حضرت شریح فرماتے ہیں کہ کسی آدمی کی گواہی پر گواہی دینا جائز ہے حقوق میں، چنانچہ حضرت شریح گواہوں سے کہتے تھے، کہو مجھ کو عادل نے گواہ بنایا ہے (ب) میں نے حضرت شعی" سے پوچھا کوئی آدمی کسی آدمی کی گواہی پر گواہ بناتا ہے۔ پس وہ ایک خط لاتا ہے جو میری تحریر کے مشابہ ہے، اور مہر لاتا ہے جو. میرے مہر کے مشابہ ہے۔ اور مجھے یاد نہیں ہے کہ وہ میری تحریر ہے تو حضرت شعمی نے فرمایا گواہی مت دو جب تک کہ یاد نہ آئے ( ج ) حضرت اسود نے اپنی قوم کو کہتے ہوئے سنا کہ حضرت علی نے نابینا کی ایک چوری کے بارے میں گواہی رو کی ، اس کو جائز قرار نہیں دیا۔
[2822] (13) And it is not permissible for a witness, when he sees his handwriting, to testify unless he remembers the testimony. [2823] (14) And the testimony of a blind person is not accepted. There is a report about it: From Shurayh: He said, 'The testimony of a man concerning a man in rights is permissible.' And Shurayh says to the witness: 'Say: a just man made me a witness.' (Musannaf Abd al-Razzaq, Chapter on Testimony of a Man Concerning a Man, vol. 8, p. 1338, no. 15447) In this report it is that he should say: 'A just man made me a witness.' From this it is understood that one can become a witness only if appointed. [2822] (13) And it is not lawful for a witness, if he sees his handwriting, to testify unless the testimony is remembered. Explanation: A person sees his handwriting in which testimony was written, but he does not remember the full event; then testifying only by seeing the handwriting is not permissible. Yes, if the full event is recalled, then he can testify. Handwriting resembles handwriting; it is possible that someone else wrote it and he thinks it is his handwriting. Therefore, without remembering the testimony, he should not testify by seeing the handwriting. (2) There is a report: He said: I asked al-Sha'bi: I said: A man makes me a witness on the testimony of a man, and then he brings a book that resembles my writing and a seal that resembles my seal, and I do not remember. Al-Sha'bi said: Do not testify until you remember. (Musannaf Abd al-Razzaq, Chapter on the Witness Who Recognizes His Handwriting but Does Not Remember It, vol. 8, p. 1354, no. 15517; Sunan al-Bayhaqi, Chapter on the Ways of Knowledge of Testimony, vol. 10, p. 266, no. 20588) From this report it is understood that as long as the event is not remembered, he should not testify by seeing handwriting. (2823) (14) And the testimony of a blind person is not accepted. Explanation: Testimony (shahada) is derived from shahid (witness), meaning giving testimony based on seeing. Therefore, in matters where testimony is given based on seeing, the testimony of a blind person is not accepted. However, in matters where testimony is given solely based on hearing, Imam Abu Yusuf's opinion is that the testimony of a blind person is accepted. There is a report: Al-Aswad ibn Qays al-Anzi heard his people say that Ali rejected the testimony of a blind person in a theft case and did not validate it. (Sunan al-Bayhaqi, Chapter on the Ways of Knowledge of Testimony, vol. 10, p. 266, no. 20586; Musannaf Abd al-Razzaq, Chapter on the Testimony of a Blind Person, vol. 8, p. 324, no. 15380) From this report it is understood that the testimony of a blind person is not accepted. (3) The hadith says: 'Do not testify until it becomes as clear as the sun.' And a blind person cannot see, so for him it will not become as clear as the sun; therefore he cannot testify. The hadith is from Ibn Abbas. Footnote: (a) Hadrat Shurayh says that testifying on a man's testimony is permissible in rights. Accordingly, Hadrat Shurayh used to tell witnesses: 'Say: A just man made me a witness.' (b) I asked al-Sha'bi: A man makes me a witness on the testimony of a man. Then he brings a book that resembles my writing and a seal that resembles my seal, and I do not remember that it is my writing. Al-Sha'bi said: 'Do not testify until you remember.' (c) Hadrat Aswad heard his people say that Hadrat Ali rejected the testimony of a blind person in a theft case and did not validate it.
Source pages p. 147

Commentary
This passage contains two distinct rulings. First, [2822] deals with a witness who sees his own handwriting containing testimony but does not recall the event itself. The ruling is clear: he cannot testify based solely on recognizing his handwriting. The reason is that handwriting can be forged, and certainty (yaqin) is required for testimony. The support comes from the report of al-Sha'bi, who explicitly advises not to testify until memory is refreshed. Second, [2823] addresses the testimony of a blind person. Since shahada linguistically derives from 'seeing' (mushahada), the general rule is that a blind person's testimony is not accepted in matters requiring visual observation, such as theft or sale. However, Imam Abu Yusuf makes an exception for matters based on hearing (like acknowledgment or divorce). The passage provides a report from Ali rejecting the testimony of a blind man, and connects this to the earlier hadith that testimony requires clarity like the sun, which a blind person cannot achieve through sight.

Key Terms
الخط (al-khatt): Handwriting; specifically, the written record of a testimony.
تذكر الشهادة (tadhakkur al-shahada): Recalling the actual testimony from memory, distinct from recognizing the document.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
A witness finds a document in his own handwriting containing a testimony but does not remember the incident. According to the Hanafi school, can he testify?
A) Yes, because his handwriting is proof.
B) No, because he must remember the testimony itself.
C) Yes, if the document is notarized.
D) No, because he was not formally appointed.

Key Takeaway
Testimony requires certain knowledge (yaqin); recognizing one's own handwriting without memory does not meet this requirement.

Testimony of a Blind Person in Hanafi Fiqh
Ruling with proof and intra-madhhab difference

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the general Hanafi position on a blind person's testimony and distinguish between visual and hearing-based matters, including the intra-madhhab difference of Imam Abu Yusuf.

Core Idea
A blind person's testimony is not accepted in visual matters, but Abu Yusuf allows it in hearing-based matters.

This lesson examines the testimony of a blind person. The linguistical connection between 'shahada' and 'mushahada' (visual witnessing) leads the Hanafi school to generally reject a blind person's testimony in matters requiring sight. However, Imam Abu Yusuf makes an exception for matters based solely on hearing, such as acknowledgments or divorce. We will study the proofs and the practical implications.

Guided Path
1
State the general Hanafi position
The testimony of a blind person is not accepted in matters that require visual observation (e.g., theft, sale, assault). The word 'shahada' itself implies seeing.
The passage states: 'And the testimony of a blind person is not accepted.'
2
Identify the proofs
The passage provides multiple proofs: (1) the report from Ali rejecting a blind man's testimony in a theft case; (2) the hadith that testimony requires clarity like the sun; (3) the linguistic derivation. These establish the general rule.
These proofs are from the athar and hadith mentioned in the commentary.
3
Note the intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf
Imam Abu Yusuf differs: he accepts the testimony of a blind person in matters that are heard, such as acknowledgments (iqrar), divorce (talaq), and other auditory events. Abu Hanifa and Muhammad al-Shaybani maintain absolute rejection.
The text explicitly says: 'Imam Abu Yusuf's opinion is that the blind person's testimony is accepted in matters solely based on hearing.'
4
Determine the mufta bihi
The relied-upon position is that of Abu Hanifa and Muhammad al-Shaybani (general rejection), but in practice, Abu Yusuf's view is considered for hearing-based cases, especially when the blind person's testimony is the only evidence.
The tarjih authority is not explicitly given in this text.
5
Apply to a scenario
A blind person hears a man pronounce divorce to his wife. He can testify about the divorce according to Abu Yusuf, but not according to the majority. The mufta bihi may allow it if the testimony is credible.
The key distinction: visual vs. auditory matters.

[۲۸۲۲) (۱۳) اور نہیں حلال ہے گواہ کے لئے اگر وہ اپنا خط دیکھے یہ کہ گواہی دے مگر یہ کہ گواہی یاد ہو۔ تش ایک آدمی نے اپنا خط دیکھا جس میں گواہی لکھی ہوئی تھی لیکن گواہی کا پورا واقعہ یاد نہیں ہے تو صرف خط دیکھ کر گواہی دینا جائز نہیں ہے۔ ہاں پورا واقعہ یاد آ جائے تو اب وہ گواہی دے سکتا ہے۔
خط خط کے مشابہ ہوتا ہے۔ ہو سکتا ہے کسی اور نے خط لکھا ہو اور یہ سمجھتا ہو کہ یہ میرا خط ہے۔ اس لئے گواہی یاد ہوئے بغیر خط دیکھ کر گواہی نہ دے (۲) اثر میں ہے۔ قال سألت الشعبي قلت يشهدنى الرجل على الرجل بالشهادة فاوتي بكتاب يشبه کتابی و خاتم يشبه خاتمی و لا اذكر فقال الشعبي لا تشهد حتى تذكر (ب) (مصنف عبدالرزاق ، باب الشاهد يعرف کتابہ ولا یذکرہ ، ج ثامن، ص ۱۳۵۴، نمبر ۱۵۵۱۷ رسن للبیہقی ، باب وجوه العلم بالشهادة ، ج عاشر ص ۲۶۶، نمبر ۲۰۵۸۸) اس اثر سے معلوم ہوا کہ جب تک واقعہ یاد نہ آئے تو خط دیکھ کر گواہی نہ دے۔ (۲۸۲۳) (۱۴) اور اندھے کی گواہی قبول نہیں کی جائے گی۔
تشریح شہادت شاہد سے مشتق ہے یعنی دیکھ کر گواہی دینا اس لئے جن باتوں میں دیکھ کر گواہی دینا ہوتا ہے اس میں نابینا کی گواہی مقبول نہیں ہے۔ البتہ جن باتوں میں صرف سن کر گواہی دینا ہوتا ہے ان میں امام ابو یوسف کی رائے یہ ہے کہ نابینا کی گواہی مقبول ہے۔ اثر میں ہے۔ حدثنا الاسود بن قيس العنزى سمع قومه يقولون ان عليا رد شهادة اعمى في سرقة لم يجزها (ج) (سنن للبیہقی ، باب وجوه العلم بالشهادة ، ج عاشر ص ۲۶۶، نمبر ۲۰۵۸۶ / مصنف عبد الرزاق، باب شهادة الاعمی ، ج ثامن ، ص ۳۲۴، نمبر ۱۵۳۸۰) اس اثر سے معلوم ہوا کہ نابینا کی گواہی مقبول نہیں ہے (۳) حدیث میں ہے کہ سورج کی طرح روشن ہو جائے تب گواہی دو اور نا بینا دیکھ نہیں سکتا اس لئے اس کے سامنے سورج کی طرح روشن نہیں ہوگا۔ اس لئے وہ گواہی بھی نہیں دے سکتا۔ حدیث یہ ہے۔ عن ابن عباس
حاشیہ : (الف) حضرت شریح فرماتے ہیں کہ کسی آدمی کی گواہی پر گواہی دینا جائز ہے حقوق میں، چنانچہ حضرت شریح گواہوں سے کہتے تھے، کہو مجھ کو عادل نے گواہ بنایا ہے (ب) میں نے حضرت شعی" سے پوچھا کوئی آدمی کسی آدمی کی گواہی پر گواہ بناتا ہے۔ پس وہ ایک خط لاتا ہے جو میری تحریر کے مشابہ ہے، اور مہر لاتا ہے جو. میرے مہر کے مشابہ ہے۔ اور مجھے یاد نہیں ہے کہ وہ میری تحریر ہے تو حضرت شعمی نے فرمایا گواہی مت دو جب تک کہ یاد نہ آئے ( ج ) حضرت اسود نے اپنی قوم کو کہتے ہوئے سنا کہ حضرت علی نے نابینا کی ایک چوری کے بارے میں گواہی رو کی ، اس کو جائز قرار نہیں دیا۔
[2822] (13) And it is not permissible for a witness, when he sees his handwriting, to testify unless he remembers the testimony. [2823] (14) And the testimony of a blind person is not accepted. There is a report about it: From Shurayh: He said, 'The testimony of a man concerning a man in rights is permissible.' And Shurayh says to the witness: 'Say: a just man made me a witness.' (Musannaf Abd al-Razzaq, Chapter on Testimony of a Man Concerning a Man, vol. 8, p. 1338, no. 15447) In this report it is that he should say: 'A just man made me a witness.' From this it is understood that one can become a witness only if appointed. [2822] (13) And it is not lawful for a witness, if he sees his handwriting, to testify unless the testimony is remembered. Explanation: A person sees his handwriting in which testimony was written, but he does not remember the full event; then testifying only by seeing the handwriting is not permissible. Yes, if the full event is recalled, then he can testify. Handwriting resembles handwriting; it is possible that someone else wrote it and he thinks it is his handwriting. Therefore, without remembering the testimony, he should not testify by seeing the handwriting. (2) There is a report: He said: I asked al-Sha'bi: I said: A man makes me a witness on the testimony of a man, and then he brings a book that resembles my writing and a seal that resembles my seal, and I do not remember. Al-Sha'bi said: Do not testify until you remember. (Musannaf Abd al-Razzaq, Chapter on the Witness Who Recognizes His Handwriting but Does Not Remember It, vol. 8, p. 1354, no. 15517; Sunan al-Bayhaqi, Chapter on the Ways of Knowledge of Testimony, vol. 10, p. 266, no. 20588) From this report it is understood that as long as the event is not remembered, he should not testify by seeing handwriting. (2823) (14) And the testimony of a blind person is not accepted. Explanation: Testimony (shahada) is derived from shahid (witness), meaning giving testimony based on seeing. Therefore, in matters where testimony is given based on seeing, the testimony of a blind person is not accepted. However, in matters where testimony is given solely based on hearing, Imam Abu Yusuf's opinion is that the testimony of a blind person is accepted. There is a report: Al-Aswad ibn Qays al-Anzi heard his people say that Ali rejected the testimony of a blind person in a theft case and did not validate it. (Sunan al-Bayhaqi, Chapter on the Ways of Knowledge of Testimony, vol. 10, p. 266, no. 20586; Musannaf Abd al-Razzaq, Chapter on the Testimony of a Blind Person, vol. 8, p. 324, no. 15380) From this report it is understood that the testimony of a blind person is not accepted. (3) The hadith says: 'Do not testify until it becomes as clear as the sun.' And a blind person cannot see, so for him it will not become as clear as the sun; therefore he cannot testify. The hadith is from Ibn Abbas. Footnote: (a) Hadrat Shurayh says that testifying on a man's testimony is permissible in rights. Accordingly, Hadrat Shurayh used to tell witnesses: 'Say: A just man made me a witness.' (b) I asked al-Sha'bi: A man makes me a witness on the testimony of a man. Then he brings a book that resembles my writing and a seal that resembles my seal, and I do not remember that it is my writing. Al-Sha'bi said: 'Do not testify until you remember.' (c) Hadrat Aswad heard his people say that Hadrat Ali rejected the testimony of a blind person in a theft case and did not validate it.
Source pages p. 147

Commentary
This passage contains two distinct rulings. First, [2822] deals with a witness who sees his own handwriting containing testimony but does not recall the event itself. The ruling is clear: he cannot testify based solely on recognizing his handwriting. The reason is that handwriting can be forged, and certainty (yaqin) is required for testimony. The support comes from the report of al-Sha'bi, who explicitly advises not to testify until memory is refreshed. Second, [2823] addresses the testimony of a blind person. Since shahada linguistically derives from 'seeing' (mushahada), the general rule is that a blind person's testimony is not accepted in matters requiring visual observation, such as theft or sale. However, Imam Abu Yusuf makes an exception for matters based on hearing (like acknowledgment or divorce). The passage provides a report from Ali rejecting the testimony of a blind man, and connects this to the earlier hadith that testimony requires clarity like the sun, which a blind person cannot achieve through sight.

Key Terms
شاهد (shahid): Witness; one who gives testimony based on personal knowledge.
شهادة (shahada): Testimony; the act of bearing witness in court.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, in which type of case might a blind person's testimony be accepted?
A) Theft, if he heard the theft occur.
B) Divorce, if he heard the pronouncement.
C) Sale, if he touched the goods.
D) Assault, if he heard the victim scream.

Key Takeaway
A blind person's testimony is generally not accepted in visual matters, but there is scope for acceptance in hearing-based matters according to Imam Abu Yusuf.

Testimony of a Blind Person: General Rule and Exception
Ruling with proof and intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the general Hanafi ruling on a blind person's testimony, identify the exception for auditory matters per Abu Yusuf, and cite the precedent from Ali used as proof.

Core Idea
A blind person's testimony is rejected in visual matters, but Abu Yusuf accepts it for hearing-based facts.

This passage addresses the admissibility of a blind person's testimony in court. The general rule is non-acceptance because testimony (shahada) etymologically requires sight. However, the Hanafi school recognizes a significant intra-madhhab difference: Imam Abu Yusuf allows it in matters based solely on hearing, such as acknowledgments or divorces. The text supports its ruling with a report from Ali rejecting a blind man's testimony in a theft case.

Guided Path
1
Identify the general ruling
State the default ruling for the testimony of a blind person: it is not accepted (ghayr maqbul).
The text begins with 'ولا تقبل شهادة الاعمى'.
2
Locate the etymology
Recognize that shahada is derived from mushahada (seeing), so testimony in visual matters requires sight.
The commentary explains this derivation.
3
Note the intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf
Identify that Imam Abu Yusuf makes an exception for matters based solely on hearing, such as divorce or acknowledgment.
Abu Hanifa and Imam Muhammad hold absolute non-acceptance.
4
Examine the dalil
Analyze the report from Ali: he rejected the testimony of a blind man in a theft case, indicating non-acceptance in visual matters.
The report is narrated by al-Aswad and found in Sunan al-Bayhaqi.
5
Apply the distinction
Given a scenario (e.g., theft vs. divorce), determine whether the blind person's testimony would be accepted according to the Hanafi school.
Visual matters: not accepted; auditory matters: accepted per Abu Yusuf.

[۲۸۲۳ (۱۴) ولا تُقبل شهادة الاعمى.
تشریح شہادت شاہد سے مشتق ہے یعنی دیکھ کر گواہی دینا اس لئے جن باتوں میں دیکھ کر گواہی دینا ہوتا ہے اس میں نابینا کی گواہی مقبول نہیں ہے۔ البتہ جن باتوں میں صرف سن کر گواہی دینا ہوتا ہے ان میں امام ابو یوسف کی رائے یہ ہے کہ نابینا کی گواہی مقبول ہے۔ اثر میں ہے۔ حدثنا الاسود بن قيس العنزى سمع قومه يقولون ان عليا رد شهادة اعمى في سرقة لم يجزها (ج) (سنن للبیہقی ، باب وجوه العلم بالشهادة ، ج عاشر ص ۲۶۶، نمبر ۲۰۵۸۶ / مصنف عبد الرزاق، باب شهادة الاعمی ، ج ثامن ، ص ۳۲۴، نمبر ۱۵۳۸۰) اس اثر سے معلوم ہوا کہ نابینا کی گواہی مقبول نہیں ہے (۳) حدیث میں ہے کہ سورج کی طرح روشن ہو جائے تب گواہی دو اور نا بینا دیکھ نہیں سکتا اس لئے اس کے سامنے سورج کی طرح روشن نہیں ہوگا۔ اس لئے وہ گواہی بھی نہیں دے سکتا۔ حدیث یہ ہے۔ عن ابن عباس
حاشیہ : ( ج ) حضرت اسود نے اپنی قوم کو کہتے ہوئے سنا کہ حضرت علی نے نابینا کی ایک چوری کے بارے میں گواہی رو کی ، اس کو جائز قرار نہیں دیا۔
[2823] (14) And the testimony of a blind person is not accepted. Explanation: Testimony (shahada) is derived from shahid (witness), meaning giving testimony based on seeing. Therefore, in matters where testimony is given based on seeing, the testimony of a blind person is not accepted. However, in matters where testimony is given solely based on hearing, Imam Abu Yusuf's opinion is that the testimony of a blind person is accepted. There is a report: Al-Aswad ibn Qays al-Anzi heard his people say that Ali rejected the testimony of a blind person in a theft case and did not validate it. (Sunan al-Bayhaqi, Chapter on the Ways of Knowledge of Testimony, vol. 10, p. 266, no. 20586; Musannaf Abd al-Razzaq, Chapter on the Testimony of a Blind Person, vol. 8, p. 324, no. 15380) From this report it is understood that the testimony of a blind person is not accepted. (3) The hadith says: 'Do not testify until it becomes as clear as the sun.' And a blind person cannot see, so for him it will not become as clear as the sun; therefore he cannot testify. The hadith is from Ibn Abbas. Footnote: (c) Hadrat Aswad heard his people say that Hadrat Ali rejected the testimony of a blind person in a theft case and did not validate it.
Source pages p. 147

Commentary
This passage focuses on the testimony of a blind person. The general ruling is non-acceptance because shahada etymologically requires sight (mushahada). The text provides a report from Ali rejecting the testimony of a blind man in a theft case, supporting the majority Hanafi position. However, it also records the intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf: Imam Abu Yusuf opines that in matters based solely on hearing (like testimonies of acknowledgment, divorce, or the like), a blind person's testimony is acceptable because hearing suffices. The passage then links this to the earlier hadith requiring clarity like the sun: a blind person cannot achieve such clarity through sight, thus cannot testify in visual matters. The footnote reiterates Ali's rejection. The commentary emphasizes that the ruling is not absolute; it depends on the nature of the fact to be proven.

Key Terms
الأعمى (al-a'ma): A blind person; one who lacks the sense of sight.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

D) Testimony in sales contracts (visual).

Key Takeaway
The testimony of a blind person is generally rejected in visual matters, but Imam Abu Yusuf's acceptance in auditory matters is a recognized and operative exception within the Hanafi school.

Testimony of a Blind Person
Madhhab dispute on blind testimony

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the Hanafi position on the testimony of a blind person and distinguish it from the Shafi'i position by identifying the thamarah al-khilaf.

Core Idea
A blind person can testify only to what he perceives through hearing, not to visual events, because testimony requires certainty akin to seeing the sun.

The validity of a blind person's testimony raises important questions about the requirements of perception and certainty in Islamic evidence law. The Hanafi school, relying on a hadith that demands clarity like sunlight, restricts the blind to testifying on matters perceptible by other senses. This lesson examines the dispute with Imam al-Shafi'i, who focuses on the witness's state at the time of the event.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position
Identify the Hanafi ruling: a blind person cannot testify to visual matters but can testify to matters known through hearing if he is rational.
The core is that the testimony must be based on clear perception at the time of testifying.
2
Identify the opponent and their view
Imam al-Shafi'i holds that if the witness was sighted at the time of witnessing, later blindness does not invalidate the testimony.
The Shafi'i position emphasizes the initial perception.
3
Follow the opponent's proof
The Shafi'i argument: the person had certainty when he saw the event, and blindness does not erase that memory.
Their dalil is based on the principle that the act of witnessing is complete before blindness.
4
Analyse the Hanafi response
The Hanafi school argues that the hadith requires clarity at the time of testimony, and blindness prevents the necessary verification.
They cite the hadith of Ibn Abbas: 'Do not testify except regarding a matter as clear as the sun.'
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
The practical difference: Hanafi rejects a blind person's testimony on visual events even if witnessed before blindness; Shafi'i accepts it.
This affects courtroom procedure in Hanafi legal systems.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قال ذكر عند رسول الله الا الله الرجل يشهد بشهادة فقال: اما انت يا ابن عباس! فلا تشهد الا على امريضئ لک كضياء هذه الشمس وأومى رسول الله الله بيده الى الشمس (الف) ( سن لیبقی ، باب التحفظ في الشهادة والعلم بها، ج عاشر ، ص ۲۶۳ نمبر ۲۰۵۷۹) اور نابینا کے سامنے سورج کی روشنی کی طرح واضح نہیں ہو گا اس لئے وہ گواہی نہیں دے سکتا۔ نا امام شافعی فرماتے ہیں کہ گواہ کی چیز دیکھتے وقت دیکھنے والا ہو چاہے گواہی دیتے وقت نابینا ہو تو مقبول ہے۔ وقال الشعبي تجوز شهادته اذا كان عاقلا، وقال الزهرى ارأيت ابن عباس لو شهد على شهادة اكنت ترده؟ (ب) ( بخاری شریف، باب شهادة الاعمی و نکاحه وامره وانکاحه ومبايعته وقبوله فی التاذین و غیره و ما یعرف بالاصوات ،ص۳۶۳، نمبر ۲۶۵۵/مصنف عبدالرزاق، باب شهادة الائمی، ج ثامن، ص ۳۲۳، نمبر ۱۵۳۷۶) اس اثر سے معلوم ہوا کہ نابینا کی گواہی جائز ہے۔
He said: Mention was made before the Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) about a man who frequently testifies. He said: 'As for you, O Ibn Abbas, do not testify except regarding a matter that is as clear to you as the light of this sun.' And the Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) pointed with his hand to the sun (a). (Sunan al-Bayhaqi, chapter on caution in testimony and knowledge of it, vol.10, p.263, no.20579) And for a blind person, it will not be as clear as sunlight, therefore he cannot testify. Then Imam al-Shafi'i says: If the witness was sighted at the time of witnessing, even if he is blind at the time of testifying, it is acceptable. And al-Sha'bi said: His testimony is permissible if he is rational. And al-Zuhri said: Do you see that if Ibn Abbas were to testify based on [hearing] a testimony, would you reject him? (b) (Sahih al-Bukhari, chapter on testimony of a blind person, his marriage, his command, his giving in marriage, his sale, his acceptance in the call to prayer, etc., and what is known by voices, p.363, no.2655 / Musannaf Abd al-Razzaq, chapter on testimony of the blind, vol.8, p.323, no.15376) From this athar it is understood that the testimony of a blind person is permissible.
Source pages p. 148

Commentary
This passage discusses the validity of a blind person's testimony. The hadith from Ibn Abbas indicates that testimony must be based on certainty equivalent to seeing the sun. The apparent meaning suggests a blind person cannot achieve such certainty, so his testimony is not accepted. However, Imam al-Shafi'i argues that if the person was sighted when witnessing the event, his later blindness does not invalidate the testimony. The author then quotes al-Sha'bi and al-Zuhri, who accept the testimony of a blind person if he is rational or if he testifies based on what he heard. The Bukhari reference includes 'what is known by voices,' indicating that a blind person can testify to matters known through hearing. The author concludes based on these effects that the testimony of a blind person is permissible. The Hanafi position is that a blind person's testimony is accepted in matters that do not require sight, such as recognizing voices, but not in visual matters. The ikhtilaf with Shafi'i is whether blindness at the time of testimony affects previously witnessed visual events.

Key Terms
أعمى (a'mā): A person who is blind, lacking eyesight.
شهادة (shahādah): Legal testimony in court to establish a right or fact.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, a blind person's testimony is accepted in which case?
A) For any matter he claims to know
B) Only for matters he saw before becoming blind
C) For matters known through hearing, like recognizing voices
D) It is never accepted

Key Takeaway
A blind person can testify only to matters he perceives through senses other than sight, because testimony requires certainty akin to seeing the sun.

Testimony of a Slave: Dispute of Acceptance
Presenting the ruling and disagreement on slave testimony

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the Hanafi position on the testimony of a slave and evaluate the opposing evidence from early scholars.

Core Idea
The testimony of a slave is rejected because Quranic 'min rijalikum' implies free men.

The legal capacity of a slave to testify in court has been a point of disagreement among early Muslims. The Hanafi school, relying on a specific interpretation of the Quran and the practice of many Companions, holds that slave testimony is inadmissible. This lesson examines the evidence on both sides and clarifies why the Hanafi position is considered stronger.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position
Clearly articulate the ruling: the testimony of a slave (both male and female) is not accepted in court.
This is the opening statement in the passage.
2
Identify the primary Hanafi dalil
Locate the Quranic verse (2:282) and the interpretation of Mujahid that the address 'min rijalikum' specifically refers to free men.
The verse is أَشْهِدُوا شَهِيدَيْنِ مِن رِّجَالِكُمْ.
3
Examine the supporting athar
List the authorities (Ali, al-Hasan, al-Nakha'i, al-Zuhri, Mujahid, Ata') who explicitly rejected slave testimony.
The passage cites multiple sources from Sunan al-Bayhaqi and Musannaf Abd al-Razzaq.
4
Present the opposing view and its evidence
State that Anas, Shuraih, Zurara, and Ibn Sirin accepted testimony if the slave is trustworthy, with Ibn Sirin's exception for a slave against his master.
The opposing dalil is based on the general principle of accepting testimony from an adl person.
5
Analyze the Hanafi response and tarjih
Understand that the Hanafi response emphasizes the explicit qualification in the verse and the lack of full legal capacity in slavery, which creates potential bias.
The Hanafi school follows the majority of early authorities, maintaining the plain meaning of the text.

۲۸۲۴ (۱۵) ولا المملوک مملوک کی گواہی مقبول نہیں ہے۔ اثر میں ہے۔ فقال والله عزوجل يقول واستشهدوا شهيدين من رجالکم آیت ۲۸۲، سورة البقرة) افتجوز شهادة العبيد فبين مجاهد ان مطلق الخطاب يتناول الاحرار ۔ دوسری روایت میں ہے۔عن على والحسن والنخعی والـزهـري ومـجـاهـد وعطاء لاتجوز شهادة العبيد (ج) (سن للبيتي ، باب من رد شهادة العبيد ومن قبلها ، ج عاشر ص۲۷۲، نمبر ۲۰۶۰۸ / مصنف عبدالرزاق، باب شهادة العبد يحق والنصراني يسلم والعمی مبلغ ، ج ، امن ، ص ۱۳۴۶، نمبر ۱۵۴۸۶) اس اثر سے معلوم ہوا کہ غلام اور باندی کی گواہی مقبول نہیں ہے۔ بعض اثر سے معلوم ہوتا ہے کہ غلام کی گواہی مقبول ہے۔ اثر میں ہے۔ وقال انس شهادة العبد جائزة اذا كان عدلا ، واجازه شريح وزرارة ابن اوفى وقال ابن سيرين شهادته جائزة الا العبد لسيده (و) ( بخاری شریف، باب شهادة الاماء والعبید، ص۳۶۳، نمبر ۲۶۵۹) اس اثر سے معلوم ہوا کہ مملوک کی گواہی جائز ہے۔
2824 (15): And not the slave. The testimony of a slave is not accepted. There is an athar: He said: Allah Almighty says: 'And call to witness two witnesses from among your men' (Surah al-Baqarah, verse 282). So Mujahid explained that the absolute address includes free men. In another narration: From Ali, al-Hasan, al-Nakha'i, al-Zuhri, Mujahid, and Ata' that the testimony of slaves is not permissible (c) (Sunan al-Bayhaqi, chapter on those whose testimony is rejected and those whose testimony is accepted, vol.10, p.272, no.20608 / Musannaf Abd al-Razzaq, chapter on testimony of a slave who buys, a Christian who converts, and a blind person who matures, vol.?, p.1346, no.15486). From this athar it is understood that the testimony of a male slave and a female slave is not accepted. Some athar indicates that the testimony of a slave is accepted. There is an athar: Anas said: The testimony of a slave is permissible if he is trustworthy, and Shuraih and Zurara ibn Awfa permitted it, and Ibn Sirin said: His testimony is permissible except the testimony of a slave for his master (d) (Sahih al-Bukhari, chapter on testimony of female slaves and male slaves, p.363, no.2659). From this athar it is understood that the testimony of a slave is permissible.
Source pages p. 148

Commentary
This passage addresses the legal capacity of a slave to testify. The Hanafi position is that the testimony of a slave (whether male or female) is not accepted. The proof is the Quranic verse 'from among your men' (min rijalikum), which Mujahid interprets as addressing free men, excluding slaves. Additionally, several sahaba and tabi'un (Ali, Hasan, Nakha'i, Zuhri, Mujahid, Ata') are reported to have rejected it. However, there is contrary evidence: Anas, Shuraih, Zurara, and Ibn Sirin accepted the testimony of a slave if he is trustworthy (adl), though Ibn Sirin made an exception for the slave testifying on behalf of his master. The passage presents both sides but the ruling number 15 begins with 'ولا المملوک', indicating the relied-upon position is non-acceptance. The author notes the disagreement but the overall context suggests the Hanafi school follows the majority of early authorities in rejecting it.

Key Terms
مملوك (mamlūk): A slave, a person owned by another.
عبد (ʿabd): Male slave, same as مملوك.
عدل (ʿadl): Trustworthy, just; a person of upright character whose testimony is accepted.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi ruling on the inadmissibility of slave testimony is based on the Quranic condition of freedom for witnesses.

Shahadat — Testimony
intermediate
8 min
Testimony of a Qadhdhaf After Repentance: Perpetual Rejection
Dispute on accepting testimony of qadhdhaf after tawba

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on the testimony of a qadhdhaf after repentance and explain the key proof from Qur'an and hadith that supports perpetual rejection.

Core Idea
A qadhdhaf's testimony is permanently rejected — even tawba does not restore it in this world according to the Hanafi school.

This lesson explores a classical inter-madhhab dispute: can a person who was punished for falsely accusing someone of zina (qadhf) ever have his testimony accepted in court after he repents? The Hanafi school, relying on the explicit wording of the Qur'an, holds that his testimony is forever rejected. The Shafi'i school, citing the exception clause and the practice of Umar, argues that repentance restores trustworthiness. Let us examine the proofs and the response.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi Position
Identify the Hanafi ruling: the testimony of a qadhdhaf is never accepted, even after sincere repentance. This is the mufta bihi position in the Hanafi school.
The ruling applies to any legal testimony, not just cases related to zina.
2
Analyse the Primary Proof: Qur'an 24:4
Examine the verse: '...and never accept their testimony' (la taqbaloo lahum shahadatan abada). The word 'abada' (ever) indicates a perpetual, unconditional prohibition. Understand how Hanafis interpret the exception clause (illa) that follows.
The exception is seen as referring to forgiveness in the Hereafter, not to legal capacity.
3
Understand the Shafi'i Counterargument
Imam al-Shafi'i points to the same verse's exception: 'except those who repent...' (illa alladhina tabu). He argues this is general and includes acceptance of testimony. Also he cites the practice of Umar ibn al-Khattab who said 'Whoever repents, his testimony is accepted.'
This is a classic case of a general exception ('amm) versus a perpetual ('abada) restriction.
4
Evaluate the Hanafi Response
The Hanafis rebut by noting that 'abada' is explicit and limits the exception to the afterlife. They also bring an athar from Hasan al-Basri: 'His testimony is never accepted, and his repentance is between him and his Lord.' This confirms the worldly rejection.
The hadith from Aisha also lists the hadd-punished person among those whose testimony is rejected, without mentioning repentance.
5
Note the Thamarah al-Khilaf
The practical consequence: In Hanafi courts, the testimony of a qadhdhaf is inadmissible in any case, forever. In Shafi'i courts, after he retracts the false accusation and repents, his testimony becomes acceptable.
This difference affects all future litigation involving the person.

A man accused a woman of fornication and could not produce witnesses, so the hadd of qadhf was imposed on him. Even if he repents, his testimony is not accepted. The verse says: his testimony will never be accepted. 'And those who accuse chaste women then do not bring four witnesses - flog them eighty lashes and never accept their testimony, and those are the defiantly disobedient, except those who repent after that and correct themselves, then indeed Allah is Forgiving and Merciful' (Surah An-Nur 24:4-5). This verse says: never accept the testimony of one punished for qadhf. (2) Hadith: 'Aisha said: The Messenger of Allah said: The testimony of a treacherous man or woman is not permissible, nor of one who has been flogged as a hadd punishment, nor of one who bears enmity.' This hadith indicates that the testimony of one upon whom hadd has been imposed is not accepted. And if he repents, i.e., retracts his accusation, still his testimony is not accepted; the proof is this athar: 'Yunus informed from al-Hasan who said: His testimony is never accepted, and his repentance is between him and his Lord.' This athar shows that even after repentance his testimony is not accepted. Imam Shafi'i says: When the qadhdhaf repents, i.e., says 'I falsely accused that woman,' then his testimony is accepted. In the mentioned verse, 'except those who repent after that and correct themselves, then indeed Allah is Forgiving and Merciful' (Surah An-Nur 24:5) indicates that if he repents, Allah will forgive, i.e., he becomes eligible for testimony. (2) In Sahih Bukhari it is narrated: 'Umar flogged Abu Bakra, Shibl ibn Ma'bad, and Nafi' for accusing al-Mughirah, then asked them to repent, and said: Whoever repents, his testimony will be accepted.' And Abdullah ibn Utbah and Umar ibn Abd al-Aziz permitted his testimony. Muhammad al-Shabi and Qatada said: If he retracts himself, he is flogged and his testimony is accepted. Footnotes: (a) Those who accuse chaste women then do not bring four witnesses - flog them eighty lashes and never accept their testimony, they are defiantly disobedient, except those who repent after that and correct themselves, then Allah is Forgiving and Merciful. (b) He said: The testimony of a treacherous man or woman is not permissible, nor of a man or woman who has been flogged as hadd, nor of one who holds enmity. (c) Hasan al-Basri said: The testimony of one who has been flogged for hadd is never accepted, and his repentance is between him and his Lord. (d) Umar flogged Abu Bakra, Shibl ibn Ma'bad, and Nafi' for accusation against al-Mughirah, then asked them to repent and said: Whoever repents, his testimony will be accepted. Abdullah ibn Utbah and Umar ibn Abd al-Aziz permitted his testimony. Al-Sha'bi said: If he retracts himself and hadd is imposed, his testimony will be accepted.
Source pages p. 149

Commentary
This passage addresses the testimony of a person who has been punished for false accusation of zina (qadhf). The Hanafi position is that even after repentance, his testimony is never accepted in any legal matter. The author begins by stating the ruling directly: if a man accused a woman of zina and failed to produce four witnesses, he receives the hadd punishment of eighty lashes, and thereafter his testimony is rejected forever, even if he repents. The primary proof is the Qur'anic verse (Surah An-Nur 24:4) which explicitly says 'and never accept their testimony' — the word 'abada' (ever) indicates perpetual rejection. The verse's exception 'except those who repent' is interpreted by the Hanafis as pertaining to forgiveness in the Hereafter, not to acceptance of testimony in this world. A supporting hadith from Aisha lists those whose testimony is rejected, including one who has received a hadd punishment. An athar from Hasan al-Basri explicitly states that his testimony is never accepted and his repentance is only between him and his Lord. The opponents, led by Imam Shafi'i, argue that the exception clause in the verse ('except those who repent') applies to testimony as well: after repentance, the qadhdhaf becomes trustworthy again and his testimony should be accepted. They also cite the practice of Umar ibn al-Khattab who flogged some individuals for qadhf, then asked them to repent and said whoever repents his testimony is accepted. The Hanafi response, as implied in the commentary, is that the prohibition is eternal ('abada') and the exception is for afterlife forgiveness, not legal testimony. The athar from Hasan al-Basri and the interpretation of 'abada' support the Hanafi view. The text concludes with footnotes clarifying the verses and hadith.

Key Terms
حد قذف (hadd al-qadhf): The prescribed punishment (eighty lashes) for falsely accusing a chaste person of fornication without producing four witnesses.
توبہ (tawba): Repentance by retracting the false accusation (acknowledging the lie).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, what is the ruling on the testimony of a qadhdhaf (one who has been punished for false accusation of zina) after he repents?
A) His testimony becomes acceptable immediately.
B) His testimony is never accepted, even after repentance.
C) His testimony is accepted only if he receives the hadd punishment again.
D) His testimony is accepted after one year of good conduct.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school holds that the testimony of a qadhdhaf is permanently rejected, even after repentance, based on the Qur'anic word 'abada' (ever) and supporting hadith and athar.

Shahadat — Testimony
intermediate

Testimony of Close Relatives: Parents, Children, and Spouses
Ruling on testimony of close relatives with hadith and athar proofs

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on testimony between parents and children, and between spouses, and identify the hadith and athar evidence that support it.

Core Idea
Testimony between close relatives is rejected due to the inherent suspicion of partiality (tuhma).

This lesson covers a fundamental rule in Islamic evidence law: the testimony of certain close relatives is not accepted in court. The Hanafi school prohibits testimony between parents and children (including grandparents and grandchildren) and between spouses, because the natural bond of affection raises a legal presumption of bias. We will examine the ruling, its rationale, and the textual proofs from hadith and athar.

Guided Path
1
Identify the parties involved
Determine which relationships are included: parent for child, child for parent, grandparent for grandchild, grandchild for grandparent, and spouses for each other.
The ruling covers both ascendants and descendants, as well as husbands and wives.
2
Understand the legal reason (sabab)
The reason for rejection is the strong suspicion (tuhma) of partiality due to close familial or marital ties. This suspicion is considered legally irrebuttable.
Individual integrity does not remove the presumption.
3
Locate the dalil: hadith
Identify the hadith from Aisha (RA) that lists those whose testimony is not accepted, including relatives and the qani' (dependent).
The hadith is from Tirmidhi and others.
4
Locate the dalil: athar
Identify the athar from Ibrahim al-Nakha'i that explicitly enumerates the categories: parent for child, child for parent, woman for husband, husband for wife, etc.
This athar is recorded in Musannaf Abdur Razzaq and Musannaf Ibn Abi Shayba.
5
Apply the ruling to a hypothetical
Given a scenario (e.g., a father testifying for his son in a property dispute), state the ruling and cite the reason.
Practice using the legal maxim: 'al-umur bi-maqasidiha'? No, here the maxim is 'al-tuhma tu'addi ila al-radd'.

۱۲۲۶) ولا شهادة الوالد لولده وولدولده ولا شهادة الولد لابويه واجداده ۲۸۲۷] (۱۸) ولا تُقبل شهادة احدى الزوجين للآخر.
[۱۲۸۲۶ (۱۷) اور نہ والد کی گواہی اپنے بیٹے کے لئے اور نہ اپنے پوتے کے لئے ، اور نہ بچے کی گواہی اپنے والدین کے لئے اور اپنے دادا کے لئے۔
والد اور والدہ کی گواہی اپنے بیٹے اور پوتے کے لئے مقبول نہیں ہے۔ اسی طرح لڑکا یا لڑکی اپنے والدین کے لئے یا اپنے دادا دادی کے لئے دے تو قبول نہیں کی جائے گی۔ لڑکا اپنے باپ، دادا کی گواہی دے یا باپ، دادا بیٹے یا پوتے کی گواہی دے تو اس میں رعایت کرنے کی تہمت ہے اس لئے ان لوگوں کی گواہی مقبول نہیں ہے (۲) حدیث میں ہے ۔ عن عائشة قالت قال رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم لا تجوز شهادة خائن ... ولا القائع اهل البيت لهم ولا ظنين فى ولاء ولا قرابة، قال الفزارى القانع التابع (الف) (ترندی شریف، باب ماجاء فیمن لا تجوز شهادته، ج۲، ص ۵۵، نمبر ۲۲۹۸) اس حدیث میں ہے کہ قرابت والوں کی گواہی مقبول نہیں۔ اور لوگوں کی آپس میں قرابت ہے اس لئے ان کی گواہی مقبول نہیں ہے۔ پھر حدیث میں یہ بھی ہے کہ گھر کے قانع یعنی گھر والے جس کی کفالت کرتے ہوں اس کی گواہی مقبول نہیں ہے۔ اور باپ بیٹے کی کفالت کرتا ہے۔ اسی طرح بوڑھاپے میں بیٹا باپ کی کفالت کرتا ہے اس لئے ان کی گواہی بھی مقبول نہیں ہے (۳) اثر میں ہے۔ عن ابراهيم قال اربعة لا تجوز شهادتهم الوالد لولده، والولد لوالده ، والمرأة لزوجها، والزوج لامرأته، والعبد لسيده، والسيد لعبده، والشريك لشريكه في الشيء اذا كان بينهما ، واما فيما سوى ذلك فشهادته جائزة (ب) (مصنف عبدالرزاق، باب شهادة الاخ لاخيه والا بن لابيد والتزوج لامراته ، ج ثامن ، ص ۱۳۴۴، نمبر ۱۵۴۷۶ر مصنف ابن ابی هیته ۴۲۵ فی شهادة الولد لوالده، ج رابع، ص ۵۳۲، نمبر ۲۲۸۵) اس اثر سے بھی اس کی تائید ہوتی ہے کہ باپ کی گواہی بیٹے کے لئے اور بیٹے کی گواہی باپ دادا کے لئے مقبول نہیں ہے۔ [۲۸۲۷) (۱۸) اور نہیں قبول کی جائے گی میاں بیوی میں سے ایک کی گواہی دوسرے کے لئے۔
بیوی شوہر کے لئے گواہی دے یا شوہر بیوی کے لئے گواہی دے تو قبول نہیں کی جائے گی۔
(۱) یہاں بھی تعلق ہے اس لئے شبہ ہوگا کہ حمایت میں گواہی دے رہا ہے اس لئے مقبول نہیں ہے (۲) او پر ترمذی شریف کی حدیث گزری جس میں تھا ولا قرابہ ، کہ قریب خاص کی گواہی مقبول نہیں ہے۔ اس لئے بھی مقبول نہیں ہوگی (۳) اور یہ اثر بھی گزرا۔ والمرأة
حاشیہ : (الف) آپ نے فرمایا خیانت کرنے والے کی گواہی جائز نہیں۔ نہ گھر کے غلام کی اور نہ ولاء میں شریک کی اور نہ قرابت والوں کی ۔ حضرت فزاری نے فرمایا قانع سے مراد نو کر اور تابع ہے (ب) حضرت ابراہیم نے فرمایا چار آدمیوں کی گواہی جائز نہیں ہے۔ والد کی اپنے بچوں کے لئے، اور بچے کی والد کی لئے ، عورت کی شوہر کے لئے ، اور شوہر کی بیوی کے لئے ، اور غلام اپنے آقا کے لئے ، اور آقا کی اپنے غلام کے لئے ، اور شریک کی شریک کے لئے جس مال میں دونوں شریک ہیں۔ بہر حال ان کے علاوہ تو اس کی شھادت جائز ہے۔
[12826] (17) And not the testimony of a parent for his child and his grandchild, nor the testimony of a child for his parents and his grandparents. [12827] (18) And the testimony of one spouse for the other is not accepted. The testimony of a father and mother for their son and grandson is not accepted. Similarly, a boy or girl giving testimony for their parents or grandparents is not accepted. If a boy testifies for his father or grandfather, or a father or grandfather testifies for his son or grandson, there is suspicion of favoritism, so their testimony is not accepted. (2) Hadith: Aisha said: The Messenger of Allah said: 'The testimony of a treacherous person is not permissible... nor of the qani' of the household, nor of one suspected regarding wala' or kinship.' Al-Fazari said: al-qani' is the dependent. This hadith states that the testimony of relatives is not accepted. Since there is kinship between these individuals, their testimony is not accepted. Also in the hadith: 'the qani' of the household' meaning one whom the family supports, his testimony is not accepted. A father supports his son, and in old age a son supports his father, so their testimony is also not accepted. (3) Athar: Ibrahim said: 'Four (types) whose testimony is not permissible: a parent for his child, a child for his parent, a woman for her husband, a husband for his wife, a slave for his master, a master for his slave, and a partner for his partner in the property they share. But aside from that, their testimony is permissible.' This athar also supports that a father's testimony for his son and a son's testimony for his father and grandfather are not accepted. [12827] (18) And the testimony of one spouse for the other will not be accepted. If a wife testifies for her husband or a husband for his wife, it is not accepted. (1) Here too there is relationship, so there is suspicion that he is testifying out of support, therefore not accepted. (2) The hadith of Tirmidhi already passed which said 'la qarabah' (no kinship) – testimony of a close relative is not accepted, so it is not accepted for this reason as well. (3) And this athar also passed: 'wa al-mar'atu' (and the woman). Footnotes: (a) He said: The testimony of a treacherous person is not permissible, nor of the slave of the household, nor of a partner in wala', nor of relatives. Al-Fazari said: qani' means servant and dependent. (b) Ibrahim said: The testimony of four types is not permissible: a parent for his children, a child for his parent, a woman for her husband, a husband for his wife, a slave for his master, a master for his slave, and a partner for his partner in property they share. Apart from these, their testimony is permissible.
Source pages p. 150

Commentary
This passage states the ruling that testimony between certain close relatives is not accepted in Islamic courts. It covers two categories: (1) parents and children/grandchildren, and (2) spouses. The author begins by quoting the matn from al-Quduri: 'Nor the testimony of a parent for his child and his grandchild, nor the testimony of a child for his parents and his grandparents. And the testimony of one spouse for the other is not accepted.' The commentary expands on this: the prohibition includes both ascendants (father, mother, grandparents) and descendants (son, daughter, grandson, granddaughter). The reason given is suspicion (tuhma) of partiality due to close familial relationship. The author then provides three proofs: a hadith from Aisha listing those whose testimony is not accepted, including those with kinship (qarabah) and the qani' (dependent) of the household; an athar from Ibrahim al-Nakha'i explicitly listing the categories; and a second hadith. For spouses, the same reasoning applies: the marital relationship creates a strong bond, leading to suspicion of bias. The commentary notes that the hadith about kinship covers this as well. The footnote clarifies that qani' means a dependent or servant. The overall ruling is that these testimonies are invalid (ghayr maqbula).

Key Terms
والد (walid): Father or parent (includes mother as per context).
قانع (qani'): A dependent member of the household, such as a servant or someone who is supported by the family.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, is the testimony of a mother for her son accepted?
A) Yes, because a mother is not the same as a father.
B) No, because the ruling includes both parents.
C) Yes, but only if she is not supporting him financially.
D) No, because a son cannot testify for his mother either.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school rejects testimony between parents and children (including grandparents and grandchildren) and between spouses due to the legal presumption of partiality (tuhma).

Shahadat — Testimony
intermediate
6 min
Why a Parent Cannot Testify for Their Child
Ruling on parent-child testimony with proofs

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling that a parent and child cannot testify for each other and explain the proof from hadith and athar.

Core Idea
A parent’s testimony for a child is rejected due to the suspicion of bias (tuhma) arising from natural affection and dependency.

Islamic law places great emphasis on impartiality in testimony. The Hanafi school identifies certain relationships where the natural bonds of love and support create a strong likelihood of favoritism. In this lesson, we examine the prohibition of testimony between parent and child, and the foundational evidence supporting this rule.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling and its scope
Read the matn statement: 'No testimony of a parent for his child and grandchild, and no testimony of a child for his parents and grandparents.' Note that it covers both ascending and descending lineage.
This includes grandparents and grandchildren.
2
Understand the rationale (ta'lil)
The author explains that the rejection is due to 'tuhmat al-tahayuz' (suspicion of bias) because the witness naturally supports his relative.
The bias is presumed, not actual dishonesty.
3
Analyze the hadith from A'ishah
The Prophet (peace be upon him) rejected testimony of a 'qani' ahl al-bayt' (dependent of the household). Since a parent supports a child, the child is a qani'.
The hadith is from Tirmidhi and is zanni al-thubut.
4
Examine the athar from Ibrahim al-Nakha'i
Ibrahim listed four categories whose testimony is rejected, including 'a parent for his child' and 'a child for his parent'.
This athar is from Musannaf 'Abd al-Razzaq.
5
Confirm the Hanafi position
Based on the evidence, the Hanafi school holds that testimony between parent and child is invalid. No intra-school disagreement.
This is the mufta bihi position.
