Shahadat — Testimony
beginner
8 min
Testimony of a Fasiq Rejected: Quranic Proofs
Establishes the principle that a fasiq's testimony is rejected with Quranic proofs

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the two Quranic proofs for rejecting testimony of a fasiq and apply the Hanafi definition of 'adl to determine witness eligibility.

Core Idea
A witness must be 'adl; a fasiq's testimony is rejected by clear Quranic commands.

This passage opens the Book of Testimonies by establishing a foundational principle: the testimony of an open sinner (fasiq) is not accepted. The author cites two Quranic verses as evidence and clarifies the definition of a just witness ('adl) through an early authority. Understanding this principle is essential for evaluating witness eligibility in Islamic court.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Ruling
State the ruling: the testimony of a fasiq is rejected. This is the central claim of the passage.
The passage begins by listing examples (female singer, habitual drinker) but the principle applies to any fasiq.
2
Analyze the First Dalil (Quran 65:2)
Read the verse: 'And bring to witness two witnesses of justice among you...' The imperative implies that witnesses must be 'adl. The converse is that a non-'adl witness is unacceptable.
This is a dalalat al-iqtida' (implied meaning) from the command.
3
Analyze the Second Dalil (Quran 49:6)
Read the verse: 'If a fasiq comes to you with news, verify it...' The command to verify a fasiq's news shows his unreliability, which extends analogically to testimony.
This uses qiyas (analogy) from news to testimony, as both require truthfulness.
4
Define 'Adl via the Athar
The athar from Ibrahim al-Nakha'i defines 'adl as one against whom no suspicion (riba) has appeared. This means one who avoids open sin.
This definition is practical: it looks at external appearance, not hidden state.
5
Apply the Ruling to a Scenario
Consider a person known for habitual gambling without repentance. He is fasiq, so his testimony is rejected. If he repents and reforms, he may become 'adl.
Repentance restores 'adalah.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
كتاب الشهادات ) مغنيَّة ولا مدمن الشرب على اللهو ولا من يلعب بالطيور. آیت میں ہے۔ واشهدوا ذوا عدل منكم واقيموا الشهادة لله (آیت ۲ ، سورة الطلاق (۶۵) اس آیت سے معلوم ہوا کہ عادل کی گواہی مقبول ہے فاسق کی نہیں۔ اس لئے جو لوگ مسلسل گناہ کرنے کی وجہ سے فاسق ہو گئے اور ابھی بھی اس گناہ کے عادی ہیں اس سے تو بہ نہیں کی ہے تو اس کی گواہی مقبول نہیں ہوگی (۲) دوسری آیت میں ہے۔ يا أيها الذين آمنوا إن جاءكم فاسق بنبأ فتبينوا أن تصيبوا قوما بجهالة فتصبحوا على ما فعلتم نادمين ( آیت ۶ ، سورۃ حجرات ۴۹) اس آیت میں ہے کہ فاسق کوئی خبر لائے تو اس پر یقین مت کرو۔ اس کی پوری تفتیش کرو کیونکہ فاسق جھوٹ بول سکتا ہے۔ اس لئے اس کی گواہی بھی مقبول نہیں ہے (۳) عادل کی تعریف یہ ہے۔ قلت لابرهيم ما العدل من المسلمين؟ قال الذين لم تظهر لهم ريبة (مصنف عبدالرزاق ، باب لا يقبل منهم ولا جار الی نفسه ولا منین ، ج مامن میں ۱۳۱۹ نمبر ۲۵۳۶۱) اس اثر سے معلوم ہوا کہ جو گناہ کر کے مشکوک ہو چکا ہے وہ عادل نہیں رہا۔
Book of Testimonies: (The testimony of) a female singer and a habitual drinker is not accepted, nor of one who plays for amusement and one who plays with birds. In a verse: 'And bring to witness two witnesses of justice among you and establish the testimony for Allah' (Quran 65:2). From this verse, it is understood that the testimony of a just person is accepted, not that of a fasiq. Therefore, those who have become fasiq due to continuous sin and are still addicted to that sin and have not repented—their testimony will not be accepted. (2) In another verse: 'O you who have believed, if a fasiq comes to you with news, verify it, lest you harm a people out of ignorance and become regretful over what you have done' (Quran 49:6). This verse says: do not trust a fasiq when he brings news; investigate it thoroughly, because a fasiq may lie. Therefore, his testimony is also not accepted. (3) The definition of 'adl (just) is: I asked Ibrahim, 'What is justice among Muslims?' He said: 'Those against whom no suspicion has appeared' (Musannaf Abd al-Razzaq). From this athar, it is understood that one who has committed sin and become suspect is no longer 'adl.
Source pages p. 153

Commentary
This passage begins the Book of Testimonies by establishing a foundational ruling: the testimony of a fasiq (sinner) is not accepted. The author provides two Quranic proofs: Surah al-Talaq (65:2) commands calling two just witnesses, implying the opposite—a non-just witness is unacceptable; and Surah al-Hujurat (49:6) requires verification of news from a fasiq, analogously applying to testimony. The author then defines 'adl via the athar of Ibrahim al-Nakha'i: one who is not known for suspicion (i.e., not openly sinful). The practical effect: if someone habitually commits a major sin without repentance, his testimony is rejected. This is a ruling supported by Zahir al-Riwayah.

Key Terms
عادل ('adl): A Muslim who is not suspected of open sin; one against whom no suspicion has appeared.
فاسق (fasiq): One who openly commits major sins or persists in minor sins without repentance.

Key Terms from Source Passage

C) The witness must have memorized the Quran.
D) The witness must be over forty years old.

Key Takeaway
The testimony of a fasiq is rejected due to lack of moral reliability, as proven by Quranic commands and the definition of 'adl.

The Testimony of a Mukhannath: Distinguishing Effeminate Mannerisms from Major Sin
Ruling on testimony of effeminate men with proof from hadith

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on the testimony of a mukhannath and apply the distinction between mere effeminacy and active sodomy.

Core Idea
Testimony of an effeminate man is accepted unless he commits sodomy—major sin, not mannerisms, is the disqualifier.

This lesson examines the Hanafi position on the testimony of a mukhannath (effeminate man). While some may assume all effeminate men are disqualified, the school distinguishes based on whether the individual engages in the major sin of sodomy (liwat). We will explore the textual evidence from the Prophet's curse and his command to kill those guilty of sodomy.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two categories of mukhannath
Recognize that the text distinguishes between a mukhannath who engages in sodomy (liwat) and one who merely has effeminate mannerisms. This distinction is the key to the ruling.
The category matters for the hadith evidence; each scenario has a separate proof.
2
Examine the hadith on the curse of effeminate men
The hadith from Ibn Abbas reports that the Prophet cursed effeminate men and ordered their expulsion. This indicates that such behavior is sinful, but not necessarily a major sin disqualifiying testimony unless it involves a major sin like sodomy.
The curse alone does not specify the level of sin; it is combined with the sodomy hadith.
3
Examine the hadith on the death penalty for sodomy
The hadith commands killing both the active and passive participants in the act of the people of Lot. This establishes it as a major sin (kabirah) deserving death, making the perpetrator a fasiq.
The punishment indicates the severity; a fasiq's testimony is rejected.
4
Derive the ruling on testimony acceptance
Combine the two hadiths: the mukhannath who commits sodomy is a fasiq, so his testimony is rejected. The mukhannath who only has effeminate mannerisms without sodomy is not guilty of a major sin, so his testimony is accepted.
This is the mufta bihi position; other schools may differ on the acceptance of the non-sodomite mukhannath.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
مخنث گنہ گار ہے اس کی دلیل اس حدیث میں ہے۔ عن ابن عباس قال لعن النبی الله المخنثين من الرجال والمترجلات من النساء، وقال اخرجوهم من بيوتكم واخرج فلانا و اخرج عمر فلانا (بخاری شریف، باب فی اہل المعاصی داشتین ، ص ۱۰۱۰ نمبر ۶۸۳۴) اس حدیث میں محنت پر لعنت کی ہے اور اس کو گھروں سے نکالنے کا حکم دیا ہے اس لئے اس کی گواہی کیسے قبول کی جائے گی۔ اور لواطت کرتا ہو اس سے گنہگار ہونے کی دلیل اس حدیث میں ہے۔ عن ابن عباس قال قال رسول الله له من وجدتموه يعمل عمل قوم لوط فاقتلوا الفاعل والمفعول به (ابوداؤد شریف، باب فیمن عمل عمل قوم لوط ص ۲۶۵، نمبر ۴۴۶۲ ترندی شریف ، باب ماجاء فی حد اللوطی ، ص ۲۷۰، نمبر ۱۴۵۶) اس حدیث سے معلوم ہوا کہ لواطت کرنے والے اور کرانے والے دونوں قتل کر دئیے جائیں۔ اس لئے کہ یہ گناہ کبیرہ میں مبتلا ہیں۔ اس لئے یہ فاسق ہوئے اور ان کی گواہی مقبول نہیں ہے۔ اگر لواطت نہ کرواتا ہو، صرف عورتوں کی طرح چال ڈھال ہو گئی ہو تو اس کی گواہی مقبول ہے۔ کیونکہ وہ گناہ کبیرہ میں مبتلا نہیں ہے۔
An effeminate man (mukhannath) is sinful. Its evidence is the hadith: Ibn Abbas said: 'The Prophet cursed effeminate men and women who imitate men, and said: Expel them from your houses, and so-and-so was expelled, and Umar expelled so-and-so.' (Bukhari). In this hadith, the mukhannath is cursed and ordered to be expelled from houses. So how can his testimony be accepted? And if he commits sodomy (liwat), the evidence for his sinfulness is the hadith: Ibn Abbas said: 'The Messenger of Allah said: Whoever you find doing the deed of the people of Lot, kill the doer and the one done to.' (Abu Dawud, Tirmidhi). From this hadith, it is understood that both the one who commits sodomy and the one on whom it is committed are to be killed. Because they are involved in a major sin. Therefore, they are fasiq and their testimony is not accepted. If he does not commit sodomy, but merely has effeminate mannerisms like women, then his testimony is accepted, because he is not involved in a major sin.
Source pages p. 153

Commentary
This passage addresses the testimony of a mukhannath (effeminate man). The author distinguishes between two scenarios: (1) If the mukhannath engages in sodomy (liwat), he is a fasiq committing a major sin, punishable by death according to the hadith; thus his testimony is rejected. (2) If he only has effeminate mannerisms without committing sodomy, he is not guilty of a major sin, so his testimony is accepted. The proofs are the hadith of the Prophet cursing effeminate men and the hadith prescribing death for sodomy. The ruling aligns with the Hanafi principle that only persistence in major sins or open fisq invalidates 'adalah. Similarly, those who play with birds are mentioned but not elaborated—presumably because it is a form of frivolity that distracts from religious duties, but the text does not provide separate proof; it groups them with the mukhannath as those whose testimony is rejected if they are habitual sinners.

Key Terms
مخنث (mukhannath): An effeminate man; one who imitates women in speech and mannerisms.
لواطت (liwat): Sodomy; the act of the people of Lot.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the basis for rejecting the testimony of a mukhannath who commits sodomy?
A) The hadith cursing effeminate men.
B) The hadith prescribing death for sodomy.
C) Both hadiths equally.
D) The consensus of the Companions.

Key Takeaway
Testimony of an effeminate man is accepted unless he commits sodomy, which is a major sin that breaks his 'adalah.
